henry goo wracke take woorse fled kyng edward whome moost gentle sorte intertayned sone repented hym deede meane season kyng henry gotte greate power scotish menne vnwittyng edward gat duresme whiche thyng hearde duke somerset fled priuely hym greate compaign e yt kyng fredes folowyng many desire lucre vautage turne hym henry thought haue greate armie enemie whiche armie made menne thynke bee greater yt spoile destroye townes feldes soeuer came long burnyng wastyng came village called exham buckeled discomfitur henry sixt iohn marque montacute whome mette fightyng sharpely often tymes chaunsed putte flight losyng greatest noubre hoost hymself fewe ino went hast scotland residue fled one waye saue liues ther taken prisoner henry duke somerset robert duke hungerforde thomas rosse whiche duke somerset putte death duke somerset taken beheded chaunged mynde sone went ye partie newe castell ther beyng season putte death like maner wherby haue trust victorie capitaines dedde gone albeit kyng edward nowe might thynke thynges wel selfe strong enough agaynst power hys enemy gotte suche vyctorye yet dyd wyth dylygence prouyde margarete kynge henrye vi hys wife shulde hande let anye greate feare whatsoeuer chaunced muche came england dysguysed apparel beinge knowen taken certayne spyes sone come caried london king edwarde layde holde whose attachynge imprysonmente realme set quyetnes wherfore edwarde nowe beynge oute feare daunger hys enemyes dyd wholy set hym selfe foure yeres ensuynge reformatyon redressynge hys publyke weale recompensynge hys souldyers paynes deuyde geue landes theim wyth kynge henrye hys owne wyth geuynge large ample rewardes dyd get fauoure hys people well laye noble vsynge suche vrbanyte clemencye kinde men throughlye wonne harte men whyche gentylnes fryndely famyliaritee dyd euer vse also lawes realme dyd alter mend made newe besydes coyned monye wel golde syluer whyche coynynge royalles noble daye currante whyche golde royal noble syluer grotes hys tyme thys kinde coyne came vp hys realme thys state made proclamation yf anye manne beyng traytoure rebellyon hertofore hys grace wyllyng submyt hym selfe wholy hym shuld haue pardon wolde shuld die suffer according lawes kyndnes natyue loue dyd cause hym haue good wyl herte common much euydent al dayes hys lyfe conqueroure helpe ayde much hys enemyes euer shamefully put wrack reason dyd incessautlye reproue ether thys cause sedycion whyche afterwarde dyd ryse betwyxte kynge edwarde earle warwycke el pryuie enuye malice whiche theyr hertes nowe brastynge wherby occasio erle ryuers father elizabeth quene soonne iohn woduile towardes euenyng kyng edward drewe nigh heryng death soden betyng doune menne taried toune fiue myle frome place therle warwike went chief toune hoost within twoo dayes caused therle pebruch certain state taken yt tyme bee behedded meane season begonne awaie bee foud peace whiche letter wer wrytten fro herauldes sent kyng therle frome erle kyng wherby kyng trustyng verely pacified lesse ware hym self feared lesse aduersaries whiche thyng knowen shewed erle certain spy went furth night priuely could strong power kyng tentes ther killyng theim yt kepte watche tooke kyng vnware brought hym warwike entent kyng frendes might knowe wher conueighed hym priuely then night toune yorkeshire called middelame bee kepte fast hold yet kyng could bee place prisone shortely knowen whiche caused many menne bee sorie lament chaunce hym self prisone spake faire kepers castell muche intreatyng greate promise made tempte corrupt theim dimissed althoughe rumour erle willyng whiche might bee likelyhood therle gyuen ouer fightyng suche yt eiuill fortune kyng henry wherby manne maye perceiue could neuer haue purpose seyng mannes strength policie able ouercome therle fredes ventre bodyes spent substauce haue brought henry royall dignitee knewe suerly long edward reigned neither could yet kyng hery beare rule yet neuerthelesse thei lette hym goo holde kyng edward deliuered went streight yorke beyng honorably receiued citezens taried space twoo dayes gette hym hoost menne could haue worthy compaignie consideryng yt goo london emong middest hoost went frome yorke lancastre found wyllyam hastynges lord chamberlain hauyng greate helpe came safe lodon therle warwike duke thei perceiued kyng edward bee deliuered throughe meanes false trai tour thynges thei appoincted none effecte greately moued anger sorowe callyng together chief frendes consulted howe thei might begynne battaill whiche whe kyng taken hold ended dooen thus dooyng certain veray angre loue thei warre offred theim selfes fight freshe nothyng yt whiche moued ye chief capitaines ye earnest also kyng edward wyllyng fight thei wherby might either bryng theim force armes quietnes peace el destroy kylle theim euery mother soonne realme might bee tter state thorowe sedicious rebellyng people wer greately impouerished seyng churche house menne spoiled obbed menne euery place ye corne grasse also destroyed grounde many mischiefes dooen whiche dooe chaunce eftsons battaill consideracion wherof piti many menne see comen weale case whiche wet dayly hourely aswell therle kyng atonemet desieryng counselyng theim bothe thei would rather kepe peace haue loue menne quiet lyuyng liue angre enuie fightyng one yt vndooyng realme wher wer wicked deede kylle father yet greate dele wicked destroye whole bodie commen weale whiche father menne whiche euery manne maynteyned kept greate entreatyng noble menne therle kyng gyuyng feyth one peace tyme wherein erle duke went bothe london small compaignie menne comparison daunger thei wer westminster kyng reformacion stablishyng thynges peace bee wher kyng thei beeyng greate woordes nothyng determyned ended therfore kyng vowe made departed said lytle erle duke also went warwike lyncolne shire gotte vp newe hoost made sir robert welles soonne rychard welles graude capitain noble manne warre tydynges commyng london moued kyng veray sore whome thought would rather haue kepte peace warre yt shewed hym vnlokyng yt battaill hande wt muche yt sooner spede gathered armie tyme set dyuerse messe gers haroldes rychard welles thesame rychard eeyng often sent made excuse sicke diseased afterward whe excuse admitted thynkyng purge hymself sufficietly kyng came london bringyng wt hym sir thomas democke brother lawe whe certain frendes certified hym ye kyng sore moued hym whiche feare kyng take sentuarie westminster brother also mindyng tary vnto suche tyme yt kyng anger wer couled apeaced kyng edward trustyng pacifie tumulte without bloddeshede promisyng mene feith yt would harme caused theim bothe come sentuarie kyng callyng rychard hym warned hym byd brother robert leaue warre goo frome erle meane season kyng went foreward wt hoost enemy bryngyng hym foresaid rychard thomas beeyng frome stamforde wher enemy lie space twoo dayes iourney informed yt robert kepte yt armie still nothyng moued yt letter father wrytyng whiche kyng beyng sore greued caused bothe rychard thomas euen cotrarie promise moost shamefully haue heddes chopped robert whe sawe kyng drawe nigh hard father sir thomas democke put death stoode first doubte whether fight ieoperdeous ventre vpon suche greate power yt erle came yet last stoute courage manly boldenes hym thei went together fought sore long many menne killed bothe sydes last whe fore named robert encouraged menne wer ready geue ouer coumpassed enemy taken also sir thomas delalat many whiche capitaines beyng taken ye hoost putte flight driuen awaye kyng beyng glad victorie comaunded robert sir thomas delalant many bee put death yt tyme place battaill ther kylled mene reported tenne thousand menne erle tyme beeyng owne toune warwike commyng shortely armye stamforde power enformed battayle foughte quickelyer looked men worse parte although might discouraged yet made thoughe passed would beleue entente myghte enboulde certaine compaigny despayryng geuyng theimselfe flight beganne make newe hoste many faire promyses wowe brother lawe thomas stanley take parte yt said thomas would meanes fight rebell agaynste kyng edwarde seeyng tyme gooe one waye mistrustyng able resiste power hys enemyes fled wyth duke clarence soonne lawe excetre whe taried two three dayes seyng lacked al thynges necessarye warre purposed gooe lewes kyng fraunce ambassate fraunce veraye well acquaynted beloued trustyng ether haue helpe kyng el incense hym wholy fight hym toke shippe dartmouth duke greate nombre theyr familie sayled ye wynde normandie chiefe lord towne entreteyned hym royally al ye hast certified yt kyng lewes comyng thither yt kyng meruailyng greatlye yt noble actes yt erle doen mynded thorowly helpe hym yt could knewe yt laded frauce glad sent hym certayn noble shewe hym wishe haue occasion wherby might helpe hym time would gladly dooe desieryng hym come ambassy kyng laye ambassy manour place yt kynges set vpo ryuer syde loire duke also sonne law bee losse harme yt ix yere kyng edwardes reigne ix yere erle fled fraunce lorde cccc lxxx greued kyng edward thei wer fled many ye people comunaltee desyrous see hym thought sonne goone theim worlde absent suche estimacio honour people yt thei worshipped honoured none hym least none hym muche yt name euery mannes song voyce especially come people made triumphe abrode yt stretes wherby moste parte helde earle syde bare hym fauoure theyr harte kyng edward wherby ye kyng feare daunger owne countremen yt wer realme theim abrode fraunce prouide yt erle comyng first sente charles duke burgom brother law desiryng yt would manashe lewes kyng wt made league peace aide erle warkwike yt duke sonne lawe neither wt mony charles wrote yt kyng frauce thretened hym many thynges mainteyned helped theim kyng frauce red letter auswered saied yt might lawfully would sauyng league truce helpe freds yt wer valiaut noble men earle settyng nothyng thretenyng braggyng wordes sayd shoulde bee neither greate peyne coste hym whe tydynges came england yt kyng veraye sorie cause searched priuely realme wer fredes enemy feare yt reason examinacio theim yt wer prisoner hand take sentuarie came ye kynges side emonges theim lord marque montacute offered hymself kyng helpe hym warres kyng gladly receaued mo would leane side meane season ye erle warwike duke went ambassy wher kyng frauce way people came veraye thicke see hym harde muche speakyng noblenesse came kyng receaued hym moste gently shortly erle breake mynd shewed cause commyng whome kyng promysed coulde dooe hym vttermoste extente power sone quene margarete wife henrye yt vi came theim sone prince edward earle penbruck also oxeforde whiche lytle sayled ouer comuned together concernyng yt safegard body league made thorowe kyng fraunce counsel first lady anne doughter earle maried despoused prynce edwarde quenes soonne also erle duke promysed faithfullye yt woulde geue ouer vnto suche tyme kyng henrye vi edwarde soonne proclaymed kyng englande kyng henry erle duke ouersee gouerne realme wyll apoyntmente quene margarete sonne prince edwarde vnto suche tyme forenamed prince wer lawfull age habilitee whiche promysed faythfully obserue dooe wer apoynted besydes many condicions made aswel reason require busynes yt tyme league truth faithfulnes thus made kyng lewes holpe erle mene harnes nauie might surer go englade rhenate also father quene margarete gaue hym mene harnyse power hauyng small nombre men take shippe sayne mouth ther tariyng hard word englad letter come ouer haste many yt would take parte yt shoulde haue nede bryng hym wer redy harneyse water side willyng helpe hym al yt could onely many noble men prince would helpe hym wt mony men harneyse yt could dooe receaued letter purposed go forth take oportunitee tyme ye quene redy set forth duke oxeford ye duke penbruch went wt parte yt hoste nauye trie chauce thei shuld haue thinges chaunce well quene prynce folowe come vnto englande therfore earle duke thanking king highly coulde doone much theim dyd take leaue sayled vnto englande armie duke burgoyne contented earle shoulde bee holpen king frauce agaynst king edward prepared great nauye shippes aboute costes normandye might take hym coming towardes englande yet neuerthelesse earle escaped daungers landed safe menne dartmouth frome whiche place sayled fraunce halfe yere earle came lande made proclamacion king henry vi name lawfull age shoulde make battayle agaynst edwarde duke yorke whiche agaynste ryghte lawe tyme crowne whiche doon cannot spoken howe soone went aboute ye realme come made proclamacy whiche also expressed howe many thousandes menne came hym earle hauing power greate armie went streyght london whome edwarde perceyued drawe nighe fledde tyme trustyng haue hym vauntage laste dryuen ende mynde get hoste resyst enemy beyng greate daunger owne lyfe fled wt duke gloucestre brother vnto towne night sea called lye taking shippe sayled flaunders charles duke burgoyne greate daunger parell lyfe reason boisterouse cruel winde elizabeth wyfe beyng greate th childe dyd take sentuarye westmynster broughte bedde n chylde whose name edward earl newe going awaye kyng edward made haste london hearing tumulte busynesse kente village suburbes spoyled piteously lytel going awaye yt kyng pacified theim sette thinges good ordre agayne whiche benefyte louingly accepted theim doon came towre deliuered kyng henry vi prisone geuing hym robe may ye broughte hym poules people reioysing euery syde thanked god chaunsed wolde desired yere lorde iiii c foure score one kyng henry beganne reigne king henry often vanquyshed began reigne nowe likely shortely faule againe fortune chaunsed hym many mennes opinion simple innocent man yt rather godlinesse vertue excell honoure rule yt loue yt religion loked dignitee honoure whiche chaunseth fewe wil seke regard kepe haue enemy saide coward herte manlynesse bee kyng meete offyce soeuer despiseth comune people alloweth maruaileth accompted mad man contrariwyse yt doeth agree theim tale wise man dede suche wisdom comely saide foolishnesse god also saide god yt bee graundfather henry fourth gotte violencye force armes yt coulde bee longe enioyed hym faute graundesire redounde nephewes nowe yt matter king henry held parlyament westmynster xxvi daye nouembre whiche edwarde declared openly tray toure coutree bycause taken yt crowne goodes geuen away like maner al yt take parte iudgement geuen theim dye furthermore yt decree statute actes yt forenamed edward broken none effecte yt earle warwike man yt deserued much coutre made gouernoure ouer yt realme take ye duke clarence felowe hym yt meanes yt realme brought new state cleane transformed altered parliament came lorde marque mountacute excusing treason yt take kyng edward parte saing feare death pardone truely yf man taken kyng edwardes part stand side manly sore enemie hurted much frendes false fained coloured frende thinges ware knewe bee pernicious dooe lesse hurte v nowe quene margarete fraunce prayed euery daye time earle went england victorie whiche knewe obteined king letter came shortely take shyppe towardes england thorowe yt sharpnesse wether greate tempestes constrayned lande differre iourney tyme tyme gaspar earle penbruch went wale earledome founde lorde henry earle richemonde brother sonne chylde ten yere olde kepte prysoner lyke noble man ye erle willyam harberte wyfe whome spake edwarde made hym erle taken batayl behedded comaundement earle warwike henry whiche richard king vii thirde brother edward ouercome vanquished gouernaunce realme whome bee beleued came kingdo sent one god quench put awaye greate sedicion stryfe betwixte henry edwarde seyng minded nothyng muche whome lady margarete onely doughter iohn fyrste duke somerset dyd bryng beyng fourtene yeres age whiche althoughe maryed henry duke bucking ham sonne earle derby yet neuer broughte chylde thought doone parte hadde borne manne chylde kynge realme gasper earle penbruch tooke thys chylde henrye earle harberte hys wife brought hym soone london king henry syxte whome kynge beeholded longe holding hys peace maruailing goodlye wytte chylde sayde thys wyse noble tyme present loo thys thys saye whome wee oure aduersaries shall geue place prophecye henrye vi kyng henry vii possession thys prophecied self henry shuld tyme come chaunsed dede haue kyngedome rule realme nowe edwarde althoughe oute countree yet dyd dyspayre shulde haue mattre redy occasion recouer kingdome duke burgoyne partlye promised hym greate ayde socoure partly priuy frendes englande dyd councell hym letter sente tyme time yt would hasten iournay homward incontin tly many fled hym oute englande eyther feare lawes offended elles sorowe worlde turned could haue theyr wyll accomplyshynge theyr couetouse myndes desyres caused hym make haste homewarde kynge edwarde beynge rauished golden promise thoughte nothyng payneful wretched tary one daye lenger nothyng pleasaunt go iourney takynge moo wyth two thou sande harnesed menne sprynge yeare sayled englande landynge coastes yorkeshyre hauen towne called rauinsport settynge hys menne dyd reason wyth hys captaynes consulte place shoulde fyrste goo ieoperdious consydering small companie take anye waye longe delyberation agryed certayne knightes horseman smal compaignie shuld bee sent one euerie quarter townes wer nyghe intente myghte drawe harte myndes people king edwardes syde lykelye kynge edwarde beyng wyse manne durst bolde would wyse come england small power excepte knowen surely haue great helpe hys commyng whych plain token duke clarence lorde marque procured hys fauoure promysinge helpe coulde make tryall whych ther manifest token dysclosed bewrayed falshed priuilie wet know mennes mindes parte would declyne nexte day came kinge edwarde shewed common people dyd stande stiflye kynge henrye syde woulde defende hys quarell ryghte iuste al time nomore nede nowe make anye tumulte much manne would althoughe eftsons desired prayed go king edward yea noman woulde feare earle warwike heare anye thinge spoken matter whose myndes kinge edwarde throughlye serched knowen chaunged mynd purpose wher claymed crowne publyrshed abrode woulde haue hys ryghte landes heritage yorke shyre worde cannot well spoken howe redily wer willinge helpe consideringe claymed nothinge hys ryghte somuch pytie dyd moue manye althoughe woulde helpe hym yet hande resyste kynge edwarde reconsilyng selfe common people meanes toke hys iournye towarde yorke wente beuer lay earle beinge warwik knew yt king edward landed york streyght sent post brother lord motacute liyng winter pomfreit wt great army shewe daunger mighte ensue yf king edward got yt towne york bed theim yf enemy drewe nigh ether mete plain felde elles bete theim towne vnto tyme came wyth greater host prepared hast coulde knew surely way enemy wolde come fyrst sent euery towne york shyre yorke selfe certayne postes bid euery man harnesse ready yt citezins shut gate surelye kynge edward myght haue accesse meane tyme king edward came peaceably wythoute resistaunce anye man towardes towne yorke whose commyng citezens certified made sure gate standynge harnesse defence dyd sende twoo alderman warne kyng comming nyghe dooe enterpryse farre put hym selfe ieopardie mynded dryue hys awaye wyth power myghte edwarde heard theyr myndes greate feare agonie could tell dooe yf shuld haue goone back feared common people men gredye praye woulde persue yf goo forth daunger yorke shyre men leaste shoulde sodenlye faull vpon hym take hym therefore seeyng able match battayle thought mollyfie theim fayre wordes beganne entreat lowlye gentle maner messaungers woulde hys name shewe cytezyns came clayme crowne hys herytage ryghte yorke shyre therfore woulde helpe theyr lorde duke yorke yf myghte receaued theyr meanes wolde requyte theyr kindenes remember theyr benifyte longe lyued suche fayre speaking flatterie dimissed folowed straighte gate companie citezins beynge somwhat moued wyth thys answer entended harme agaynst kyng henrie spake wyth hym wall badde hym go frome thence would go quickely take harme speakyng veraye gentely euerye one theim callyng name moost gentely desire theim yt might come owne toune passyng daye comunicacion yt length citezens partely ouer come wt moost getle speakyng large promise made fell poincte yt edward would swere handle citezens gentle sorte hereafter bee obedient kyng henry comaundement thei would receiue hym yt citee helpe hym wt yt power thei might edward beyng glad next daye early masse said ye gate wher receiuyng sacrament promised feithfully vpon othe yt would obserue bothe thynges afore named receiued citee neuerthelesse ferre vnlike would obserue one theim minded none thyng yt might depriue kyng croune shall appere euidet yt ofte tymes se noble men aswell laye people thorowe ambicion filthy couetousnes thei forgettyng god godlynes dooe swere greate othes promisyng thynges ye whiche entendyng thei make othe breake shortely yet suche person oftymes haue rewardes god one tyme edward tyme punishment falleth nephewes offence vncle comitted thyng speake rychard third place wher manne maye see ye progenie edward wer punished offence edward thus framed matter forgettyng ye othe yt made se yt citee strogly kepte gettyng hym army together thought wold lynger busines bycause harde enemy made greate preparauce haste tooke iourney towarde london goyng purposely goo waye yt led hym pomfret wher ye lord marque toke yt right hand within lesse iiii mile enemy whe perceiued yt thei made skyrmishe mocion came right waie past theim wet notynghame greued yorke shire mene deceiue theim vnhonestly otherwise become kyng noble manne knowen kyng edward came wt daunger enemy notyngham came hym many noble mene vpon consideracion yt lord mou tacute either would entre vpo enemy though agreed theim el durst come tentes able matche wt theim therfore menne thought better take edwardes part consideryng yt power greate hold kyng henry hee daunger liues losse goodes landes edward reioysyng went lecestre hearyng therle toune warwicke therle oxenford hym hauyng greate armie thei bothe entended bryng hym theim preuentyng purpose wet awaye wt hoost either wyllyng fight el ioyne frendeship loue brother duke clarence whome commyng fro london wt hoost mene thought speake yt came therle copaignie fearyng leste yt would stand yt promise yt made yt variable incostat ye meane tyme therle warwike heuie sore moued wt ye lord marque would neither kepe kyng yorke bed yet thei came nose would proffer theim one fight therfore cosideryng yt enemy multiplied gooyng towardes hym made hoost sent yt duke clarence come hym hauyng hoost london whe perceiued linger man doubtyng whether kepe battaill peace haue mind settyng forth mistrusting also yt traine allured folowe brother take partes tooke waye couetrie thende might meete enemy edward came warwike frome then erle pitched tentes hym next daie bad battaill therle whiche erle durst come oute feare duke clarence whome thought deceaued hym duke deede came shewed greate power menne whiche edward perceaued made towardes hym bee thought bee made guyle sette hoost araye though would fight duke thei came sight richard duke gloucestre one take vp matter firste spake duke priuely eare came edward hym laste peace proclaimed wherby euery manne puttyng doune weapon edward brethre enbraced louyngly one edward made bee proclaimed yt duke theim came hym bee perpetuall frendes thei three loue like thre brother thei wer brotherly loue euer neuer thelesse god dooeth seme haue forgiue edward offece periury although eue nowe fortune fauored hym yer long vexed wt werre beside yt plage distrucio child death thei wer thus come together thei minded proue yt erle wold come theim also hold wt theim ye duke clarece set certain frendes yt whiche first shuld excuse yt done desire hym yt would bee one kyng edward whose mynde whe therle heard vtterly detested hym muche cursyng cryed oute hym yt contrary feith othe made fled kyng edward comaudemet biddyng yt set made none aunswer rather bee like hym self like false periured duke yt appoincted vtterly neuer leaue battaill either wer killed ded enemy ouercomed edward hauyng suche strong power mene went boldely london wher knowen duke clarence taken parte brother come one knot citezens suche feare thei could tell dooe lengthe dryuen feare take kyng edward parte thesame tyme came letter earle kyng henry yt duke somerset yt archbyshop yorke kyng counsel yt kepe citee enemy handes space ij iij dayes would come streyght great armye mene defended citee strongely coulde purpose citezens cosyderyng ye kyng henry greate warryer yt small policie feates thesame contrary wise kyng edwarde man hym selfe coulde rule realme maruelous well suche man woulde onelye preserue hym selfe also defende theim maner iniuryes harmes shoulde chaunce thought best leane syde commyng london people coulde thretenyng strayt comaundement otherwyse kepte backe would mete hym comyng salute hym altogether kyng ruler realme whose commynge duke somerset certayn fled away made beste shifte euery manne hym selfe could escape hades sauyng kyng ry taryed poste alone bishoppes paleyce besyde powles standynge lyke desperate manne knowynge dooe taken kyng edward cast pryson agayn towre edward came london xi day apryll halfe yere hadde sayled flaunders callyng councel together highly commende citezens yt faythfulnesse bare hym especiall alderman yt caused people obeysauce hym also sharpelye rebuked cytie knewe haue lent monye kyng henry yt cause woulde haue made theim paye mony preparyng hoste hym last bad theim bee without feare promysyng theim pardon safetie life thorowe whiche gentlenesse gatte fauoure comen people wonderfully erle consideryng battayll shortelye folowed enemyes great haste entente yf enemy stoppe lette yt waye myght fight buckel theim came lo pursued theim long came good waye iourney worde brought yt edwarde gotte london imprisoned kyng earle perceauyng victorie ende fightyng tryed one batayle rested saynt albones partely refreshe men partely take counsayl hoste duke excester earle oxenforde duke somerset lorde mountacute marque brother earle earle perceaued bee vnwyllyng fight agaynst kyng edward therfore trust hym yet loue yt betwixte brother brother diminished suspicion whatsoeuer thought eyther hym hymselfe euer feare daunger came saynt albones toune halfe waye betwyxte london aboute tenne myle frome london called barnet toune standeth hyll goodlye playne earle entended pitche battayle edward hearyng prepared armye adioyned greate power young menne theim bowes bylles speares arowes maner instrumentes apperteynyng warre furnysshed menne thought make riddauce theim tyme fynishe battayle longe holden came armye mete enemy might bee redier fight theim wheresoeuer mette theim foure wynges could escape hym hand brought hym battayle also henry prisoner entente aduersaries might bee discouraged sight hym el fortune fauoured hym might neuerthelesse bee saued noone pytched tentes fore named barnet nighe hys enemyes myghte fyghte daye defended hys tentes veraye strongelye longer taryed better reason daylye concourse noble men commen people hym woorse earle farre frendes lodged night breake day ye earle warwike bega araye armye sorte fyrste lorde marque earle oxenforde set lefte syde wyth certayn horssemen hymselfe duke exceter ryght syde myddeste betwixte theim bothe setteth duke somerset archer thus araiyng theim battayl beganne exhorte theim thei would fight lustely lyke hardye meune reuengyng quarell countree moste falsely possessed yt croune like maner kyng edward whiche set theim ordre encouraged theim fight lykewyse remembre thei inuaded rebelles traytours sedicious person whiche entended nothynge vtter destruccion losse theyr countree daye came trompettes beganne blowe bothe sydes token ligne battayle firste bowe men shot drawynge nere tryed sweorde edwarde trustyng thorowe multitude haue better stade stiffely theim enbouldenyng souldiours coulde whose power erle moste manfully resisted long cotinuaunce battail many men wer slayne whose place succeded euer fresher fresher length erle perceauyng bee ouerthrowen kyng great power drewe nigh foreward constreyned kyng geue backe litle edward seeyng brought freshe men aide ye thother wer beten downe sore ye groude edwarde beeyng werye longe fyghtynge fought mornyng none caused theim wer without battayl standyng defece edward yf nede fall vpo enemy beare theim downe wt great power erle seyng freshe come vpo theim nothing afeard trusting loking surely victorye dyd comforte encourage menne almoste discomfited moost manfully desiring theim beare oute laste brunt lustely victorie redounde theim weryed longe continuaunce nothing moued wordes self moste valiauntly came among myddest enemyes kylled slewe many theim hym selfe laste striken downe brother lorde marque folowing hym whose deathe fled taken moste parte theim ende earle whose stoutenesse stomack made hym bee lyke peryll leopardye many time dyuerse sundrye suche conflictes warres killed partes ten thousande menne many taken prisoner could noumbred duke somerset earle oxforde entendyng take waye scotlande dyd chaunge mindes bicause farre fro theim fledde streight wale earle penbrucke euery man saue liues fledde one way erle exeter skaping hardely tooke sentuarye westminster remayned edward gotte victorye went london moost triumphyng fassion hauyng henry hym prisoner deed corp also earle lorde marque brought poules laye space ii dayes euery manne might see theim bee deed man fainyng yt aliue myght sowe sedicion againe reuenging quarel yet kyng glad ye death therle sory losse destruccion yt lord marque whome dyd esteme take great frende quene margaret hearing yt edward come englande done much hurte yt realme purposed come england soonne also prince edward wt great armye chosen picked frenchman land waimouth yt greate tempest yt see could come soone woulde landed heard kyng edward conquered husband take prisoner destitute frendes ye erle brother lord marque slaine felde army discomfyted slayne putte f ight began like piteful desperate ladye mourne lament fate calamitee husband ye whiche nowe see haue chaused sowith great feare agonie case rather dye lyue quene mighte haue thought yt euell chaunsed putting death ye duke gloucestre whose deathe althoughe peradueture giltie yet offended dyd saue suche good man yf liued dominion publike weale king henry neuer suche trouble nowe leaue yt quene despering bothe owne life sone also went therby monastery charterhouse monkes place called bewe lieu englishe called faire place ther taking sentuarie remained soonne knowen sentuarie came duke somerset brother erle deuonshire whiche man euen frome beginnyng taken parte whose returning redounded euell destruccion also erle penbroke ihon wen locke ihon longstrother capytaines ruler rhodes quene sorowe miserye somwhat comforted sighte frendes wt whome talked shewed cause yt came rather desiryng theim prouyde safegard soonne helpe nowe ye would wether serued goo fraunce againe bryng wt god willing better mature time greater power duke began putte good comforte would wise ye set mind whole vpon batail nowe fight edward whe bothe vnprepared also furnyshed men yt hable fight considering ye great batell wt therle warwike yt men sore hurted weryed together yt myght chauce haue yt better hym although discofyted therle hoste yt victorie turneth oftentymes one momet short space furthermore shewed ye part yt nobilyte bare theyr good mindes hertes kyng henry bee yt would bee capitaine bene tyme passed promised great army owne costes charge woulde make noble menne take parte defende time quene mistrusting fearing yet muche owne soonne aunswered saied allowed counsell well yf might bee daunger sonne therfore fearing fought earnestly countree soonne might bee destroied caste awaye thought best either putte differre battayl time elles sende soonne fraunce bee kepte vnto suche tyme ye better successe warres truely mother withoute cause louing chylde owne husbande prisoner captiue persone therfore one caste awaye nexte hym loued mooste tenderly soonne also might goo yt wisely aboute entente quene counsayled theim laye heedes together caste way howe conuey businesse yf would fight promised theim helpe good councell erle saied nede waste wordes woulde fight stoutely agaynste enemy therfore woulde doo might power determined apointed vpon gathered armye euery manne parte oute owne countree shire quene brought good hope warre saied wel streight went yt councell yt duke bathe looking tarieng armye place euer went would aknowen none thentent yt aduersaries might knowe vnto time came wher woulde bee edward hearyng quene come duke somerset prepared hoost ayde sente certayne spy viewe number armye shewed hym nomber yet knowyng whether wold goo kyng apoynted mete came london gathering armie went oxforde shyre pytched hys tentes abyngton encreasinge hys nomber army much could perceauyng wer bathe taryed purposely multyply enlarge company came malebrydge xv myles frome bathe hasted come go wale suspected whether dede thei entended erle penbruck hauyng theyr great bonde men toune bathe quene fled frome thence brystowe wyllinge goo glouceter sent spyes knowe yf myght haue passage whome aunswere broughte coulde thei towne would anye meanes geue place hearynge went bristowe teukisbury ther duke pytched hys battayle agaynst wyll aduise many captaynes whych counsayled hym tarye erle penbruches comyng edwarde dyd take quene kylled least imprysoned euery one almoost came nobilitee killed earle deuonshyre iohn wenlock captayn rhodes brother duke somerset wyth manye moo taken prisoner quene margaret sonne prince edward yt duke somerset yt lord ihons xx knyghtes besyde wer behedded ii dayes yt selfe towne sauyng quene margaret soonne edwarde shortelye prynce edwarde brought kyng asked wherfor inuade hys realme answered boldly sayde recouer kyngedome heritage forefather progenie dew wordes edwarde sayde nothyng thrustyng hym hys syght wyth hys hande duke clarence glouceter yt lorde hastynges dyd kyll mooste cruelly hys departyng hys mother quene caryed london prysoner fro thence raunsomed fraunce lyued perpetuall sorowe care much selfe husband onely sonne edwarde whome henry husband trusted lyue possesse ye croune kinge edward thus ouercome theim went london ther iii dayes caused procession bee euerye place moost solempne deuoute fassy last ciuile battaile king kept yere lord iiii c lxxx xi kynge edwarde returned backe subduynge hys rebelles one fauconbrydge earle kente hys basterde stoute harted manne beynge admyrall sea none shoulde passe betwixte calysse douer ayde socoure kynge edwarde appoyntemente earle warwyke dryuen nede pouertee beganne bee pyrate rouer seea much throughe robberye shamefull spoylynge gotte vnto hym greate nauye shyppes laste landed kente getting hym greate multitude kentyshemenne wyth assistence theim hys ryotouse compaignye shyppemenne came london sayde wyth lowde voyce woulde defende kynge henrye restore hym hys crowne people cytezyns london perceauyng quene margarete ouercome battayle woulde geue theim passage wyth greate myghte vyolence enforsed fawconbrydge geue backe take shyppe kylled toke prysoners better parte menne shortely fauconbridge landing vnware southampton taken behedded speake earle penbrucke whe knowne quene taken tewkesburye waged battayle goynge hys waye turned backe agayne chepstey lamentyng greatly owne chaunce also euell fortune yt kinge ry dyd breath alitle deliberate wt selfe wer best done meane time king edward set one roger vaugha take yt erle train guile erle certified take self hedded hi yt killed yt intended kyll place yt erle went toune pebrucke wher besiged thomas morgan set fro king could get oute meanes eyght daye one dauid brother forsayde morgane moost assured frende conueyed awaye went toune sea syde called tinby takynge shyppe fraunce w th lorde henrye nephewe earle rychemonde brother chaunce came britaine shewing duke cause hys comminge committed selfe wholy handes duke entertayned earle company yt best maner could made theim though bene hys brother promysing theim sure passeporte saueconduite ouer ani place rule gouernaunce nowe kinge edwarde hys realme pacified great tumultes apeaced tooke iourny rence setting iustices caused inquisicion serche made busines insurrection basterd adherentes offence manye put death suffered execution moost sharply accordig merites longafter thentent yt king edward myght bee al daugers assaultes enemy hery yt depriued log crowne also spoiled life yt killed report fame went duke glouceter suspected haue done yt dede sticked wt dagger dead corp brought vnreueretly fro towre yt stretes yt citee vnto poules ther lay yt daye morow folowing conueyed caried ye abby blak freres chertessey ther buried shortely widesore castell laied ye newe chapell george solepne toumbe henry reigned xxviii yere repossessed kyngdome halfe yeare lyued vnto lii yeres age wife quene margaret one soone called edward nowe entent yt edward kyng might liue quiet manne death went boute serche rebelles thei might bee weeded compaignie menne pernicious vnprofitable publique weale tyme tooke tharchebishop yorke brother therle warwike sent hym prisoner guynes wher long remained holde dimissed dyed shortely thought pensifulnes mynde also attached erle oxenford whiche ceason barnet felde holden sainct michaelles mounte comaundement castell beyond yt sea called hant wher remained prisoner yt space xii yeares furthermore vpo cosideracio yt rebelles traitours might haue refuge strauge coutres made league wt kyng scottes peace amitee bee obserued kepte yt xx yeares yet feare e pebruck richemond wer ye duke britain wher thei moost honorable intretainmet cosideryng also yt young erle richemod would clayme ye croune tyme come ye feare ye whiche matter sent priuie ambassadours ye duke promisyng hym yt would restore deliuer vnto hade bothe therles haue ample large porcio monye dooyng yt duke make short tale would meanes deliuer theim handes kepte theim thei neuer might bee dauger enemy hym edward therfore thirtene yere reigne whiche yere lord thousand foure hundred three score thirteen helde parlyament westminster wher first caused statute actes whiche wer abrogated henry sixt stand bee good effecte goodes traitours bestowed gyuen abrode also banished menne yt fled rebelles false countree bee brought grudge eiuill wer betwixt one nobilite ther bee forgotte turned loue lastly certain mony bee payed kyng towardes yt greate charge werre thus studied determined liue quietly set realme good ordre charles ye duke burgoin set aide hym lewes ye freche kyng yt could neuer bee rest one thyng shuld disquiet hym could deny hym helpe consideryng ye benefites yt receiued hym diuerse sudry tymes yt yt nowe fought dedly enemie whiche aided erle warwike bothe wt menne mony come hym wherfore asseblyng cousaill together shewyng theim matter sent woord duke yt would kepe one piece parte battail agaist ye kyng deede yt tyme mortall battaill betwixt duke lewes yt kyng lewes harde manne churlishe also hurtefull aswell fredes foe many frechmen abhorryng codicions consent hold yt duke emong many one lewes luceburge apoinct wt duke dooe mischief hym one waye yt kyng bothe dauger owne coutree menne also duke beyng strauger duke shewed kyng edward yt might soner allu e entise hym battaill vpo kyng edward toke voiage frauce takyng besides tribute yt certain mony ye lordes common realme thei owne getlenes gaue vn hym ye sustenauce maintenyng armie yt kyng called tribute leuiyng mony beneuolece whiche neuerthelesse giuen wt eiuill many one vsyng suche getle fassions towardes theim praiyng theim hartely assistaunce yt thei could none wise dooe geue hym whiche whe gathered armie whiche xx went caleys ye iiii daye july charles yt duke mett reioysyng gretely victory instantly desire hym would sticke stoutely battaill yt might haue yt frenche kyng yt lost hym lewes yt kyng hard edward came wt armie encreased nombre people muche could nigher daunger sooner hastely came vpon theim armie sent foorthe robert stoteuill noble capitain coostes atrebatium resyst power englishe menne kyng hym self taried siluanect castyng wt hymself waye might make league peace betwixt yt duke yt kyng england hym heryng therfore yt king gone atrebates set ambassodours hym peace whose myndes yt kyng knowe although foud litle fredship hades tymes past yet consideryng yt substauce treasure wasted ciuile battail hable maintein newe hoost nede shuld yet vnneth sustein theim vnder baner thought best eue pure necessite leaue peace growe atonemet wt lewes yt kyng whiche thyng might dooe also sauing honour cosideryng yt bothe ye duke robert luceburge aforenamed dooe accordyng promise yt desire ye ambassadours went speake kyng pinquinake toune ambia shire wher noble mene dooe asseble together found kyng bothe yt kynges due salutacio either long communicacio last peace cofirmed stablished many yeres ye emet wherof ye freche kyng gaue vnto edward toward charge cost lxcv crounes thes forth yerely l crounes yt truce made mony paid kyng edward wet caleis thes englad battaill none slain sauyng onely yt duke exceter ye whiche mane setuary comaunded folowe kyng put death cotrary yt promise made yere lord cccc lxxv frome tyme foorth lewes yt kyng payed duely raunsome edward vnto laste yere dyed tyme denyed paymente though knewe laste dayes duke burgoyne roberte lucenburgh knowen edwarde made league wyth lewes kynge freted sore hym wrote sharpe letter thretenyng tauntyng hym saiyng cause reuenged theimselfes kyng whose fyrye thundryng wordes kyng passed vpon turnyng hade lucenburgh taken prysoner proude malicious writyng behedded lutece thus kyng edward beyng quietnes countre abrode also although mighte wel thynke hymself lyue perpetually yt great conquerour yet consideryng yt erle richemode nigh affinitee ry vi feare daunger therfore thought one attempte duke britayn agayn giftes promyses faire wordes might haue erle thought rule would auncestrie geuen ambassadours came duke great substaunce mony request might bee honestier shewed duke came desire erle hym mighte marye kynges doughter affinite al euil wyll grudge might forgotten sedicion vtterlye reiected although entended cause al suche thynges bee forgotten death kyllyng hym duke longe muche deniyng theim laste thorowe although goodly sonne clerely abiected yt croune realme autorytee parliamente entayled duke yorke heyres discease sayd kyng henrye vi duke entendyng long tary myndyng vnder preterte discencion growen arysen within realme couenauntes made parliament kepte broken preuete tyme take vpon hym gouernaunce kyng henryes life muche hardynes slayne battayle wakefylde leuynge behynde hym three sonnes edwarde george richard al three wer greate estate byrth greate statelye stomake gredy autoritee impaciet parteners rule autoritee edward reueged father death deposed kyng henry vi atteyned croune sceptre realme george duke clarence goodlye well feautured prince thynges fortunate yf ether owne ambicio set brother thenuie enemy set brother agaynst hym quene ye noble bloode highly maligned kynges kynred woman comenlye malyce nature hate suche theyr husbandes loue wer aproude appetite duke hym selfe entendyng bee kyng leaste wise heynous treason layde charge finally faute fautelesse attaynted gloucestre iij sonne whiche muste mooste entreate descripcio richarde thyrde witte courage eguall beautee lyniamentes nature farre vnderneth lytle stature euill feautered lymmes croke backed lift shulder much higher right harde fauoured vysage suche estate called warlike vysage amonge commen person crabbed face malycious wrothfull enuyous reported mother duches much dooe trauayle yt could
