chauncelour englande made cardinall lyued well mennes iudgementes dyed well retourne ye former purpose long often alternate proffe aswel prosperytee aduerse fortune gotten great experience verey mother mastresse wysedome depe insight pollytike worldlye driftes whereby perceauynge nowe ye duke comen hym fed hym wt fayre woordes many pleasaunt prayses perceauyng grefe communicacions duke pryde nowe balke oute lytle brayde enuye towarde glorye kynge thereby feelynge hym easye fall oute yf matter well handled craftely soughte wayes prycke hym forwarde takynge alwayes occasyon hys commynge also keepynge hymselfe cloose wythin hys bandes rather semed folowe hym leade hym duke beganne fyrste prayse boaste kyng shewe muche profite realme take reigne byshoppe morton aunswered surely lorde folye lye sure yf woulde swere contrarye ye would beleue yf worlde would haue begone would haue wyshed kyng henryes soonne croune kynge edwarde woulde haue bene true faythfull subiecte god ordeyned hym lose kyng edwarde reigne neuer madde dead manne stryue agaynst quycke euer kynge edwarde faythfull true chapeleyn gladde would haue bene chyldren shoulde haue succeded hym howbeit yf secrete iudgemente god haue otherwyse prouyded purpose spurne agaynste prycke laboure set vp god pulleth downe late protectoure nowe kyng woorde left sauynge saide hadde alreadye medled muche worlde would daye medle booke bede ferther longed duke sore heare woulde haue sayde ended kynge sodeynlye stopped exhorted hym famylyerly betwene theim bothe bee bolde saye whatsoeuer thought whereof faythfullye promysed shoulde neuer come hurte paraduenture good woulde hym selfe entended vse hys faythfull secrete aduyce counsayle sayed onlye cause whyche procured kynge haue hym hys custodye myghte recon hym selfe home elles hadde bene putte handes theim wyth whome shoulde haue founde lyke fauoure bishoppe right humblye thanked hym sayed good faythe lorde loue muche talke prynces thynge oute perell althoughe woorde bee without faute pleaseth prince construe euer thynke isopes tale lyon proclaymed payne deathe shoulde horned beastes come wood one beaste bonche fleshe growing oute hedde fledde greate pace ye foxe sawe hym flye haste asked hym whether fledde fayth neither wote ne recke hence proclamacyon made agaynste horned beastes foole foxe lyon neuer ment whiche thou haste horne thy hedde mary wote well ynoughe yf saye horne duke laughed merely tale saied lorde warraunte neither lyon bore shall pycke matter thyng spoken shall neuer come nere care good faythe syr saied byshoppe yf dyd thyng aboute saye taken aswell god mente coulde deserue thanke yet taken wene would myghte happen turne lytle good lesse longed duke muche wherupon byshop saied good faith lord late protectoure ith kyng possessyon purpose dispute title welthe realme whereof grace hathe nowe gouernaunce wherof selfe poore membre aboute wysh good habilitees wherof hath already righte many litle nedyng prayse yet mighte haue pleased god better store haue geuen hym suche excellent vertues mete rule realme oure lord hath planted persone grace lefte againe whiche woordes duke perceauyng byshop bare vnto hym good hearte fauoure mystrusted entre plaine comunicacion hym farre ye laste byshoppe declared hym selfe bee one theim would gladly helpe richard vsurped croune mighte bee deposed knowen howe myghte conuenientely bee broughte passe ye suche persone true title inheritaunce vnto might bee restored therunto vpon saied duke knowing bishoppe bee manne prudence fidelitee opened hym whole hart entent saying lorde haue deuised ye waye howe bloodde kyng edward kyng henry syxte lefte beyng coupled maryage affinitee maye bee restored vnto ye croune iuste true title due vnto theim kyng richard called ye brother kyng edwarde fourth enemye mortall fooe waye duke deuysed shoulde spede celerytee fynde meanes sende henry earle rich mounte whome rumoure wente immediatlye vpon knowledge kynge edwardes deathe haue bene deliuered oute prysone fraunces duke brytaine henry helpe power strength saied henry woulde fyrste feithfull othe promise ymmediatly vpon obteigning croune woulde mary take wyfe elyzabeth elder doughter edward fourth byshop ely ryghte well alowed bothe deuyce purpose duke also maner waye howe matter shoulde bee broughte effecte founde meanes reynold breye seruaur margarete mother saied henry maried thomas stanley came duke wale duke mynde throughlye perceaued knowen greate spede retourned saied margarete aduertisyng thinges betwene duke hym concerning aswell comon weale realme also aduauncemente bloodde debated nowe came passe duke buckyngham ladye margaret mother saied henrye bene communicacyon matter saied lady margarete deuised meane waye deposycion kynge rycharde bringyng henry sonne whiche duke nowe brake vnto byshop ely wherupon e rested forasmuche perceaued ye duke nowe willyng prosecute sayed deuice fynde meanes matter myghte bee broken vnto quene elizabeth wyfe kyng edwade fourthe beynge sanctuarye hereupon caused one lewes physicyan owne name thoughe came hym selfe breake matter vnto quene saying yf would consent agree therunto meane might bee founde howe restore agayne ye blood kyng edwarde kyng henrye syxte vnto croune bee aduenged kynge rycharde murther kyng edwardes chyldren declared beyonde yt see henry earle richemounte whiche blood henry sixte whome yf woulde content yt marye elizabeth eldest doughter shoulde syde bee made righte many frendes parte myghte helpe lyke maner wherby doubte shoulde come passe shoulde possesse croune moost rightfull inheritaunce whiche matter heard liked excedingly well much counceled saied phisicyan breake ye vnto maistresse ladye margaret knowe mynde therein promisyng vpon woorde would make frendes kyng edwarde take parte sayed henrye yf woulde sworne came possessyon croune woulde immediately take maryage elyzabeth eldest doughter elles yf lyued tyme would take cicile yongest doughter whereupon sayde lewes retourned vnto ladye margarete hys maystresse declarynge vnto whole mynd entent quene shortly agreed betwene two wemen wyth al spede thys matter shold set forwarde much lady margarete brake thys matter vnto reynolde bray wyllynge hym moue set forwarde wt suche shoulde perceaue eyther hable doo good wyllynge thereunto quene deuysed one chrystopher whome foresayde lewes physicyan promoted seruyce shoulde bee sente brytayne henrye geue hym knowledge theyr myndes shoulde prepare apoynt hym selfe redye come wale shoulde fynde ayde helpe ynonghe readye receaue hym shortly yt came vnto knowledge duke buckingham himselfe afore entended matter whereupon thoughte yt mete sende messenger reputacyon credyte thys chrystopher kepte hym home sente hughe conewaye wyth greate monye wyllynge hym declare vnto henrye thynges hast hym come lande wale aforesayde hym one rycharde guilforde oute kente sente one thomas ramey wyth message whyche two messenger came maner bothe one tyme brytayn earle henrye declared vnto hym theyr commyssios whiche message henry perceaued throughly heard reioysed harte gaue thankes vnto god fully purposyng al conuenyente spede take iourney towardes england desiryng aide helpe duke brytayne promise thanckfull recompence god sende hym come ryghte duke britayne notwithstanding longe required thomas hutton purposely sent hym kyng richard message monye efte sone imprisone saied henry erle richemout continually kepe holde frome co minge englande yet gladnesse fauoure inclined desyre henry aided hym might menne monye shypes necessaryes henry whyle might accordynglye appoynte furnyshe hym selfe remayned brytayne sendyng afore foresayde hughe coneway thomas ramney whiche two hym trewe faithful beare tidynges englande vnto frendes commynge ende myghte prouydentlye ordre thynges aswell commodyous receauynge hym comminge also foreseynge suche daungers myghte befalle aduoydinge suche trappes snare rycharde thyrde hys complyces myght bee sette hym company bryng hym meane tyme frendes henrye care studye dilygence wroughte thynges vnto purpose belongynge thoughe secretlye wrought conueyed emonge greate nombre possible yet pryuye knowledge therof came eares kyng rychard althoughe firste hearynge muche abasshed yet thought best dyssemble matter thoughe knowledge therof whyle myghte secretly gather vnto hym power strengthe secrete spyall emonge people get perfyght knowledge whole matter chiefe autoures contryuers knewe chiefe princypal theim vnto owne conscience knewe hadde geuen moste iust cause enemytee thought necessary first dyspatche duke oute waye wherfore vnto duke addressed letter enfarced replenyshed humanytee frendshippe famylyaritee swetenesse woordes wyllyng desyryng come vnto hym conuenyent spede ferther gaue commaundemente messenger caryed letter shoulde behalfe make many high gaye promyses vnto ye duke gentle meanes persuade come vnto hym ye duke mystrustyng ye fayre woordes promyses sodenly offred hym whose wylye craftes meanes knewe sondrye exsamples afore practised desyred ye kynges perdon excusyng self deseased sicke might asserteined ye possyble wer hym come would absent hym self fro grace thys excuse kyng would admitte eftsones directed vnto ye duke letter roughe sorte wythoute manacynge threatenynge onlesse woulde accordynge hys dutye repayer vnto hym hys callynge whereunto duke plainely made aunswer woulde come vnto knewe hys enemye immedyatelye duke prepared hym selfe make warre agaynst hym perswaded hys complyces partaker hys intente wyth possyble expedycion one place another sturre agaynste kynge rycharde thys meanes maner one tyme houre thomas marque dorcester reysed armye wythin country yorke beyng hym selfe late come forthe sactuarye meanes helpe thomas rowell preserued saued frome perel death also deuonshyre edwarde courtenay wyth hys brother peter byshoppe excetter reysed lyke maner armye kent rychard guyl ford accompanied wyth certayn gentylmen caysed vp people foresayde thys done maner one moment king ye meane tyme gathered together gret power stregth thynkyng yt best pursuyng euery one hys enemyes dysparkle hys copaygnie smal flokes determyned let passe others withal whole puisaunce set vpon chiefe heade saye duke buckynghm takyng iourneye londo went towardes salisbury thentent might sette vpon ye said duke case might haue perfight knowledge ye laye felde embatailed nowe kyng within twoo dayes iourney salisbury ye duke attempted mete hym beyng accompaignied great strength welshman therunto en forced coherted lordly commaundement lyberall wage hyre whiche thyng deede ye cause thei fell hym forsooke hym wherfore beyng sodenly forsaken menne necessite constrained flee whiche dooyng manne cast sodeine therfore greate feare sodeine chaunge fortune reason thesame feare knowyng become hyde hed suche case best dooe secretly conueighed hym self hous homffraye banastar conceaued sure hope confidence finde faithfull trustie vnto hym thesame seruaunt entendyng remayne secrete vntill might either reise newe armie el meanes coueigh hym self brytein henry erle rychemount assone theothers whiche attempted thesame entrepryse ye kyng knowledge duke forsaken compaignie fled could bee foude thei beyng stryken sodein feare made euery mane hym self suche shift might beyng vtter despayre health life either gotte theim sactuaryes deserte place el assaied escape ouer sea many theim deede arryued sauely britain emong whose name ensue peter curteney bishop exceter brother edward erle deuonshire thomas marque dorcestre soonne thomas beyng verye youg chylde iho bourshere ihon welshe edward wooduyle stoute manne armes brother elizabeth quene robert willoughby gyles dawbeneye thomas harondell ihon cheiny twoo brother wyllyam berkeley wyllyam brando thomas brother rychard edgecome moste parte knightes also ihon halwell edwarde poyntz excellet good capitain christopher vrswicke ihon moorton bishop ely theself tyme together sondrye noble gentleman sailed flaundres richard kyng nowe come salisbury gotten perfight knowledge party sought slie realme dyligence hast might bee sent ye porte tounes theraboute make sure steye none theim might passe vntaken made proclamacion yt whosoeuer would bryng hym knowledge duke buckynghm bee haue rewarde bo deman frebome fre pardon besydes thousand pounde moneye furthermore vnderstode thomas hutton newely retourned oute britein afore mencioned fraunces duke brytain would onelye holde henry erle rychmount prisone sake also readie helpe thesame henry menne money shippes might hym sette dyuerse sondry shippes place conuenyent seacostes brytain ward henry come waye might either bee taken arriuall el might bee kept fro landyng coaste england furthermore euerie coaste corner ye realme laied wondrefull wayte watche take partely enemy specially thesaid duke buckynghm wherupon thesaid homffrey banaster mede losyng life goodes disclosed hym vnto kynges inquysy ymediatly tooke hym foorthwith brought hym salisbury kyng rychard duke beyng dylygently examined vttred without maner refusall styckyng suche thynges knewe trustyng plain confession haue lybertee speake kyng whiche made moste instaut humble peticion might dooe assone cofessed offence towardes kyng rychard oute hande behedded death ye duke receaued handes kyng rychard holpen affayrs purpose beyonde god forbode whyle thynges wer hand england henry erle richmount made readye hoste strength nombre fiue thousand brytones fiftene shippes ye daye apoynted departure beyng nowe come whiche ye twelfe daye moneth octobre yere lorde god thousand foure hundred lxxxiiii seconde yere ye reigne kyng richard hauyng fayre wynde hoysed vp sayles setforwarde towarde night came suche tempest thei dispersed one another britain normandy ship whiche henry one ship tossed night waues sea tempest mornyng came waxed somewhat calme faire weder thei come toward south parte england hauen porte called poole thesaid henry sawe shore bankes sette full harnessedmen whiche souldyours apoynted wayte kyng rychard haue saied comyng landyng erle henry abode gaue commaundement manne land yt comyng shippes meane tyme wayted theim sent litle bote fewe lad knowe thei stoode shore fredes enemy souldyours beeyng taught thei saie aunswered thei frendes henry appoynted ye duke buckynghm abide commyng conducte hym castelles holdes tentes pauylyons ar llary warre laie remayned hym greate power entended nowe spede set vpon kyng rychard nowe sle feare cleane without prouision therfore besought hym come alande henry suspectyng bee fraude saw none shippes apered hoysed vp satles hauyng meruelous good wynde euen apoynted hym god delyuer hym great ieopardy sayled backe agayn mandy landyng compaignie laboures arested theim space iii dayes determynyng go thence afoote brytayne meane sent messenger vnto charles frenche kynge sonne lewes lytle departed sechyng hym lybertee lycence passe thorough normady brytayn young kyng charles beeyng sory fortune onlye ready well pleased graunt passage also sent hym moneye helpe hym foorthe iourneye henry knewe kynges mynde doubtyng great humanytee gentlenes sent awaye shippes towardes britayne set hym selfe forwardes iourneye made greate haste tyll messenger retourned whiche greate gentlenes receaued kyng reioysed hearte lustye stomacke good hope set forwarde brytayne take ferther counsayle affayres brytayn receaued fro frendes englande knowledge duke buckyngham behedded marque dorcestre greate nombre ye noble men englande bene lytle seke hym wer veneti cytie brytayne whiche thynges beynge knowen erle one parte greately lament death euel chaunce chiefe princypall frende yet parte greatlye reioysed many noble menne take parte battayll therfore conceauynge good hope opinion purpose shoulde well frame come passe determyned hym selfe expedycion set foorth warde therupon wente place brytayn called rhedon thence sent marque noble men come vnto hym hearde henrye safe returned brytayne reioysed lytle thei thought landed englande fallen handes kyng richarde made lytle haste tyll wer come vnto hym whiche met greatloye gladnesse aswell parte began talke prepensed matter nowe christmasse come whiche daye altogether assembled churche sware fayth truthe one another henry sware first promysyng assone possesse ye croune england woulde marye elyzabeth doughter edward iiii warde sware feaultie homage vnto hym eue though already bene kyng tyme foorthe dyd take hym promysyng hym thei would spende bothe lyfes goodes hym richard leger reigne ouer theim dooen henry declared thynges duke britayne praiynge desyryng hym nowe helpe woulde ayde hym greater nombre menne also lende hym frendly honest somme moneye might nowe recouer right enheritaunce croune england vnto yt called desyred al lordes nobilitee realme whiche god wyllyng moste assured possesse possessio would moste faythfully restore duke promysed hym ayde vpon truste wherof beganne make redye shippes might expedicion bee redy sayle tyme loste whiche tyme kyng richard agayn retourned london taken dyuerse theim yt wer conspyracy yt say george browne roger clyfforde thomas selenger knyghtes also thomas ramme robert clyfford dyuerse caused put death called parliament wherin deereed fled oute lande reputed taken enemyes realme landes goodes bee forfayte confiscate content preade smal thyng caused also great taxe monye leuyed people ye large giftes lyberalytee first vsed buye fauoures frendshippes many brought nede nothing like yt thomas stanley shoulde haue bene reputed take one enemy woorkyng margarete wife mother vnto henry erle richemout noted ye chiefe hed worker cospyracy asmuch thought small purpose wemen coulde dooe thomas beynge nothyng fauty dely ed comauded suffre margarete wyfe haue seruautes neither yt go abroad shut vp yt thence foorth sende message neyther soonne frendes wherby hurte mighte wrought agaynst kyng whiche commaundemet accomplyshed authoryte perliament peace concluded scottes whiche lytle skyrmyshed borderer thyng brought passe ye kyng supposed conspiracye bee clene auoyded asmuche duke compaignie put death also certen bannyshed yet kyng richard daylye vexed troubled partelye mystrustynge owne strength partely fearyng commyng henrye compaignye lyued myserable case would continue lenger determyned hym selfe put awaye cause feare busynesse either pollecye elles strength hadde thus purposed hym selfe thought nothyng better tempte duke britayn yet eyther money prayer speciall rewarde yt kepyng erle henry moste chiefly knewe yt yt might delyuer hym trouble delyueryng imprisoning sayed henry wherfore incontmentlye sente vnto duke certein ambassadoures whiche promesse vnto hym besyde greate rewardes broughte theim geue hym yerely reuenues landes henry lordes beyng hym yf woulde receyte ambassadoures put theim prysone ambassadoures beynge departed come duke laye could haue communicacion hym asmuch extreme sicknesse wyttes feble weake wherfore one peter landose treasourer manne bothe pregnaunte wytte greate authoritee tooke matter hand whiche cause afterwarde hated lordes britain peter englishe ambassadoures communicacion declaring hym kynges message desyred hym instantlye asmuche knewe might bring theyr purpose passe woulde graunt vnto kyng richardes request shoulde haue yerely reuenues landes sayed lordes peter considering greatly hated ye lordes owne nacion thoughte yf myght bring passe thoroughe kyng richarde haue greate possessyons yerely reuenues bee hable matche theim well ynough care rushe theim whereupon aunswered ambassadoures would doo richard dyd desire yf brake promesse hym hatred bare vnto henry hated hym longe saued lyfe earle henry greate eoperdye suche good fortune englande craftye compacte tooke place whyle letter messenger ranne betwene peter kyng kichard iohn bishoppe ely beinge flaundres certifyed preest whiche came oute england whose name christopher vrswicke whole circumstaunce deuyce purpose wherupon spede sayed byshop caused saied preest daye cary know ledge therof britayn henry erle richemounte willing hym noble men dyspatche theim selues wt possible haste fraunce henry veneti whe heard fraud without tariaunce sent christopher vnto charles frenche kyng desiring lycence henry noble men myght safely come fraunce thing sone obteigned messenger retourned spede lorde prince earle henry setting businesse good staye ordre mighte talked lytle made fewe counsail herof expedicyon hereof caused therle penbrucke secretly cause noble men take horse dissembling ride vnto duke bretain came vttermost partes therof forsake waye led theim toward duke make fraunce euer might dooing euery thing bidde loste tyme sped theim shortely obteygned gate coutie angeou henry within ii dayes folowyng styll veneti tooke iiii fyue seruauntes hym feigned thoughe woulde haue ryden therby visyte frende forasmuche many englishmenne lefte toune manne suspected thynge kepte ryghte waye space fyue myles forsooke turned streyghte woode thereby tooke vpon hym seruauntes apparell putte apparell vpon hys seruaunte tooke one theym hym whome waited thoughe bene seruaunte maister conuenyente spedy haste sette forthe theyr iourney tyme loste made tariaunce way onelye baitynge theyr horse shortly recouered coastes angeou companye within foure dayes earle thus escaped peter receaued kyng richard confirmacion graunte promise made betreiyng henry noble wherfore saide peter sente oute hym horse menne suche expedicion spede haue taken hym scacely erle entred fraunce one houre heles englyshe menne beyng aboue noumbre thre hundreth veneti hearing earle noble fled sodeinly withoute knowledge astonyed maner despaired theyr lyues happened contrary theyr exspectacyon duke britaine taking matter vnkyndely henry bee vsed hym feare shoulde bee compelled flee lande lytle vexed peter althoughe ignoraunte fraude crafte wrought hym yet layed whole faute hym therfore called vnto hym edward poyninges edward wood vile deliuering vnto theim foresayde monye ye henrye desyred duke lende hym towarde charge iourney commaunded theim conuey conducte english menne seruauntes vnto hym paying theyr expense deliuer sayde monye vn earle earle sawe menne come hearde comfortable newes lytle reioysed desiring messenger returned shewe vnto duke trusted ere long time shewe selfe bee vnthankeful greate kyndnesse nowe shewed vnto hym within fewe dayes earle went vnto charles french kyng whome rendred thankes great benefites kind nesse receaued hym cause comming fyrste declared besought helpe ayde whiche shoulde bee immor tall benefite hym lordes whome generallye called vnto kyngdome forasmuch abhorred tiranny kyng rychard charles promised hym helpe bade good chere take care would gladly declare vnto hym beneuolence tyme charles remoued tooke hym henry noble menne whyle henry remained iohn earle oxenford whome spoken put prisone edward fourth castell hammes also iames blounte capteine castell iohn forskewe knyghte porter towne caleies came vnto hym iames capitain lefte wife ye castell dyd furnyshe good garison men departure henry sawe therle measure glad ye noble man greate experience battayl valiaunt hardie knight thought bee moste feithfull sure somuche time edward ye fourth continuall battail hym defending henry syxte thought nowe well apointed coulde desire bee better therfore comunicated vnto hym whole affaire bee ordred ruled hym longe charles frenche kyng remoued paris whome henry folowed againe moued besoughte kyng moste fauourably kindely entreteigned hym time wordes also dedes yt would lykewise please hym yet much extend fauoure beneuolence vnto hym nowe woulde ayde helpe hym forwarde iourney yt onely also lordes nobilytee englande myghte iustely haue cause knowlage confesse meane fauoure goodnesse restored againe possessyon enherytaunces whiche withoute hym coulde well bryng passe meane fortune suche ye many englyshe menne came ouerdaylye oute englande vnto many whiche paris amonge whome diuerfe studentes fell vnto parte bothe lesse specially one whose name richard foxe preest beyng manne synguler good wytte learning whome henry streyght waye reteigned comitted secretes vnto hym whome also afterward promoted many hyghe promocyons laste made hym bishop winchester richarde hearyng conspiracye greate ayde dayly wente ouer vnto henry thought yet might bring passe henry couple maryage blood king edwarde shoulde dooe well ynoughe hym kept hym possessyon croune deuysed hym selfe wayes meanes myghte bee howe bryng passe fyrste thoughte bee beste fayre woordes large promesses attempte quene whose fauoure obteygned doubted shortelye fynde meanes haue bothe doughters oute handes owne rested nothynge yf hym selfe myghte fynde meanes warde marye one doughters whereby thought shoulde make sure safe vtter disapoyntinge henrye wherupon sente vnto quene beynge sanctuarye dyuerse sondrye messenger shoulde excuse pourge hym facte afore dooen towardes settynge forthe matter plesaunte woordes hye promyses bothe also sonne thomas lorde marque dorset thynges coulde desyred messenger beyng men grauitee handled quene e ftly anone beganne bee alured herken vnto theim fauourably conclusion promysed obedient kyng request forgettyng iniuries dooen parte remembryng ye promesse made maigarete henryes mother first delyuered doughters handes kyng rychard sent preuely lorde marque sonne beyng parys wt henry ye haue heard wyllyng hym forsake henrye whome spedely returne englande thynges perdoned forgeuen fauoure frendship ye kyng highly aduauncement honoure kyng richard whe quene elizabeth thus brought fooles paradyce receaued al brother doughters sanctuary palayce thought nowe remayned nothyng dooen castyng awaye destroiyng owne wife whiche thynge wholy purposed decreed within hym selfe nothyng feared hym much mooste cruell detestable murder losyng good opynion ye thought people conceyued hym ye haue heard faigned hym selfe good thought people estemed hym euen notwithstandyng shortly foresaide vngracious purpose ouercame al honest feare first absteyned beddyng lyyng also found self greued barrenesse wife vnfruteful brought hym forth chyldren complamyng therof greuously vnto ye noble realme chieflye aboue vnto thomas rotherame archebishoppe yorke whome delyuered lytle afore oute pryson whiche byshop gather quene rid waye ere long suche experience kyng richardes complexcio practised many lyke thynges longe thesame tyme also made dyuerse secrete frendes preuy thesame coniecture caused rumoure ronne amog commen people woulde haue ye autoure knowen yt quene dead thentent yt hearyng meruelous rumour take greueous conceyt anone fall great disease would assay waye case chaunce afterward sicke dead otherwyse murdred ye people might impute death vnto ye thought tooke el ye sickenesse whe quene heard horryble rumour death sproge abroade among commen people suspected matter supposed worlde ende incontinently wente kyng lamentable countenaunce wepyng teares asked hym whether dooen thyng whereby might iudge worthy suffer death kyng made aunswere smilyng dissimulyng countenauce flatteryng woordes byddyng bee good comforte plucke vp heart suche thyng toward knewe howe euer fortuned either sorowe el poysonyng within fewe day quene dedde afterwarde buryed abbay westminster anne one rychard earle warwikes doughters whiche cotracted prince edwarde kyng ry sixt soonne kyng beyng thus delyuered wife fantasied pace ladye elizabeth nice desiryng wise mary menne yee mayden self abhorred vnlawfull desire thyng mooste detestable determined hym self make greate hast matter chiefly pecke trouble fearyng least yt noble menne would forsake hym runne vnto henry part leste would fauoure secrete conspiracy made hym ende almoost doubte also parte commen people greate dispeare many theim rather bee accompted noumbre enemy put theim selfes ieopardy bothe losse body goodes takyng parte emongest noble menne feared first thomas standley wyllyam brother gylbert talbote greate noubre whose purpose though kyng rychard ignoraunt neuerthelesse trusted one theim lest thomas standley maryed henryesanother maye well appeare fol oweth sayd thomas woulde haue departed courte vnto owne mansion recreacion saide ye truthe woulde bee readynesse receaue henry ayde hym commyng realme kyng let hym would suffer hym departe vntyll suche tyme left courte behynde hym george strange soonne heyre pledge whyle kynge richarde thus wrapped feare care ye tumulte come lo euen tydynges came henrye entred lande castell hammes prepared receiue henry meanes erle oxenforde whiche fled iames blunte keper castell vnto henry kyng rychard thynkyng begynnyng stey matter sent forth hast greater parte calyce recouer said castell castell thei sawe aduersaries make towardes theim spedely thei armed theim selfes defence al hast sent messenger hery desyryng hym ayde henry forthwith sent erle oxenforde chosen sorte menne assist theim first commyng laid siege farre castell whyle kyng rychardes menne turned backe hauyng yie towardes theim thomas brandon thirty valeaunt menne otherside gate ouer water castell strength theim within thei within laid heard charge without ye otherside erle oxenford valiantly assayled backeside thei glad make proclamacio theim within thei would content geue ouer castell thei haue free liberte departe euer thei erle oxenforde hearyng whiche came onely saue frendes hurte namely iames bluntes wife contented condicion departed saufgarde frendes returning backe henry whiche paris kyng rychard informed yt frenche kyng wery henry compaignie would doo nothyng hym wherby henry nowe hable maner helpe self possible yt shuld preuaile goo forwarde thenterprise thoughte haue taken hande agaynst kynge rycharde kynge rycharde beeyng brought thus false paradice thought hym selfe bee feare cause beynge sure one wake oute hys slepe trouble hym selfe furder therefore called backe hys nauye shyppes redy vpon sea whyche fullye furnyshed haue scoured sea yet suretie least bee sodenly oppressed gaue commaundemente greatte men dwellynge sea syde specyally welshemen watche nyghte daye leaste aduersaries shuld haue eny oportunitee entre lande fashyon time warre dwell see side make bekyns highest place whiche might bee sene afarre chaunce enemyes aryue towarde lande fyre theyr bekyns rayse countreye thentent quickely place place might ascerteyned whole matter also arme theim selfes spedelye agaynste theyr enemy come purpose agayn kyng richard thorough aforesaide tydynges beganne bee carelesse rechelesse saye power withstand desteny honge ouer hedde suche prouydent iustyce god manne dooeth leste knowe prouyde beware vengeaunce god euen hande offence go forth ye tyme henry earle richemounte remayned fraunce entretyng suyng ayde helpe frenche men many chiefe noble men realme gouernaunce young age charles kyng fel somewhat dissencion whiche variaunce lewes prynce orlyaunce chiefe hedde whiche maryed iohanne kynges syster looked haue bene chiefe gouernoure realme meanes came passe one man princypall gouernaunce realme therefore henry erle constraigned sue vnto noble seuerallye one another desyrynge praiynge theim aide helpe purpose thus matter prolonged meane tyme thomas marque dorcet whome spake afore preuely sent come home mother partely mystrustynge henrye preuayle partly greate large promesses kyng richard made hym whiche letter sayd marque receaued beleuyng thynges mother wrote vnto hym also thynkyng henry neuer preuayle frenchemen mocke daylye hym sodeynly night tyme conueyed hym selfe parys great spede made towardes flauders whiche thyng ye erle englishe lordes heard thei wer sore astonned amased spede purchased charles kyng lycence commaundement marque might steyed whersoeuer wer found wt dominion frauce chiefly secrete councel knewe purpose comaundemet quickly obteyned postes made forth euery waye emogest one humfrey cheyncy plaiyng ye parte good blooddehounde truely smelled folowed trace found toke marque handled persuaded hym gentle good woordes shortely content retourne henry beyng delyuered chaunce thought best prolonge matter farther least loose present oportunytee also wery frendes looked hym englande wherfore made haste set forewarde small army obteyned frenche kyng also borowed money frendes whiche left marque ihon burchere behynde pledge setting forward came roan whyle taryed prepared shippyng ye hauen seyne tydynges cam hym ye kyng richardes wyfe deade purposed mary lady elysabeth kyng edwardes eldest doughter nice maried cycile syster mannes sonne lade far vnderneth degre whiche thyng henry sore amased troubled thynkyng meanes al purpose dashed waye hym come kyngdome maryage one kyng edwardes doughters menes also feared least frendes englande would shrynke fro hym lacke honest title thei consulted vpon matter thei thought best cary lytle proue might gette helpe make mo frendes among thought best adioyne lord harbarte vnto theim whiche great power wale yt brought passe meanes lorde harbarte syster maryable henry would content mary would take part brig al matter passe messenger sent henry erle northhumberlande whiche maryed syster bryng matter wayes beset messenger could come hym meane season came veray good tydynges ihon ap morgan temporall lawyer whiche signified vnto theim syr ryce ap thomas noble valiaunt man ihon sauage fauoured parte earnestlye also syr reynolde braye prepared greate summe mony wage battayl parte helpe hym therfore woulde make hast euer could make towarde wale henry spedely prepared hym selfe would lynger frendes lenger made prayer vnto almightye god might haue good successe iourney two thousande menne fewe shyppes calendes august sayled hauen seyne seueth daye whiche xxii daye august aryued wale aboute sonne set laded wilforde hauen ye parte whiche called dale hearde yt dyuerse layde wayte hym kepe hym backe thence mornyng betymes remoued towarde towne called harford tene myle dale ioyfully receyued contrarye tydynges brought hearde normady afore syr ryce ap thomas ihon sauage wythal euer coulde make kyng richardes parte notwithstandynge suche tydynges sent theim fro menne pembruche valiaut gentlema whose name arnold butteler reioysed heartes whiche yf former offence might bee remitted woold bee redynesse sticke vnto owne gespare erle henryes company meanes beeyng encreased departed fro harforde fyue myle towarde cardygane refreshed menne sodenly came rumoure vnto hym lorde harbarte whiche dwelled carmerdyne nye hande greate armye menne whiche rumoure greate sturre amongeste theim euerye manne tooke hym selfe weapon made theim selfes redye nede fight lytle afrayed tyl tyme henrye sent horseman trye ye truthe whiche thei came agayn declared thynges quiet ther suche thyng moste master gryffythes verye noble man conforte theim gladden heartes whiche although ioyned hym self lorde harberte tyme cleued henry suche companye although fewe thesame tyme came ihon ap morga vnto hym henry went styll forward caried almoste place would make suer woorke better spede inuaded suche place afore thei armed hym ye whiche place bette downe wt litle stregth afterward hauyng knowlage spyes ye lorde harbert syr ryce redynes geue hym battail determyned set vpo theim either put theim flight orels make theim sweare homage feaultee vnto hym take theim wt hym hoste kyng richard woulde ascertayne frendes englande howe matter went forwad hym sent moost trustye frendes ladye margarete mother standely talbot especial frendes certain commaundementes effecte commaundementes intended helpe hys frendes passe ouer seuerne shrewesbury make toward london ther fore desyred theim councell tyme place conuenient mete hym messaungers going forth commissyons henry went forward toward shrewesbury waye mette syr rice ap thomas great noumber menne came vnto hym parte two dayes afore henry promysed hym bee chiefe ruler wale soone came croune yf would come vnto hym afterward gaue hym dede meane time messenger executing message diligetly returned back agayne large rewardes theim whome sent came henry day entred shrewesburye shewed howe frendes redynesse dooe vttermoste laye theim tidynges put henry suche greate hope went forth courage came towne newporte set vp tentes vpon lytle hyll laye night night came hym syr gylberte talbot aboue two hundreth menne went forthe stafforde whyle willyam standley came hym fewe hym talked litle retourned backe hoste whiche prepared thence went lichfelde nyght laye without toune ye morning betime entred ye citee receiued honourably daye ii afore thomas standley fyue men armed whiche knewe henry coming forthwith went afore village called aderstone tarye tyll henrye came dyd auoide suspicion beyng afraid least kyng richard knowing intent would haue put soonne deathe whiche telled lefte wt hym pledge father kynge rychard meane tyme nottingham hearing henry fewe banished men entred wale lightly regarded matter thoughte muche bee paste vpon came fewe noumbre lorde harbart sir rice wer ruler wale would kyll hym elles take hym bring hym aliue afterward remembred self oftentimes smal matter batel bee looked vnto betymes would make laste great sturre thought best remedy matter betimes commaunded henrye earle northumberlande noble realme whome thoughte set hym owne goodes rayse vp army come hym speede also sente dyuers messenger letter robert brakenburye keper towre london commaundynge hym come vnto hym haste brynge hym felowes battell thomas burschere walter hungerforde dyuerse knyghtes whome dyd litell suspecte tyme shewed henrye come shrewisburye without hurte tidinges ye kyng beganne rage made exclamacion againste theim contrary faithes vtterly deceiued hym beganne mistrust menne wiste whome mighte truste thoughte best sette forthe hym selfe ageinst aduersaryes forthwith sent spy knowe waye henry take dooen diligence retourned backe shewed hym howe henry come lichfeld thing knew greate noumbre souldyours come together menne set araye commaunded theim forwarde gooe foure foure together waye kept hearde saye enemy commynge suspecte persones putte myddes hym selfe trusted came behind winges horseman running euery syde thus keping order aboute sonne sette came vnto leicestre henrye meane season remoued lichefelde vnto nexte village called tamworth mydwaye mette walter hungerforde thomas burschier many promised aide hym afore forbecause perceyued susspected richard least brought violentlye vnto hym beyng enemye forsooke robert brakenbury capitaine nyghte tyme stale priuely awaye wente henry vnto whome chaunced waye worthy bee marked whiche henry althoughe manne noble courage also companye dyd dailye encrease yet stoode great feare vncertayne thomas standly whiche telled feare puttynge soonne deathe inclyned yet vnto parte matter sleder kyng richard reporte made hym frendes wherfore afrayde withoute cause tooke onely twenty menne steyed iourney manne dispaire halfe musynge hym selfe beste bee dooen aggrauate matter tidinges broughte hym kyng richard comming nere mete hym great houge hoste menne thus lyngered feare behinde hoste came afore toune tham worth darke night lost bothe company also waye wandryng frome place place laste came lytle village iii myle hoste full feare leste fall daunger scoute watche durste aske questyon man partly feare presente partely come laye nyght tooke sygne pronosticacyon greate plage come parte hoste lesse abashed seyng absence tyme morning henry came theim light daye excused ye matter absent lost waye rather purpose would commen wt preuy frendes would sene daye yt went priuely aderstone thomas standley willyam brother dyd dwell henry thomas willyam mette tooke hande louing salutacions glad one counceled together metyng kyng richard whome perceyued bee farre theim day drewe toward night euening ihon sauage brytanne sanforde simon digby many forsaken kyng richarde came henry wt great power men whiche thyng power strengthe sate henry alofte meane season kyng richard purposed go thorow thicke thinne mater came bosworthe alitell beyond leicestre place batell bee manne would saye hye iustice god whiche coulde bee auoided hanging ouer hed called hym place suffer worthy punyshemente detestable offenees sette vp tentes rested night afore went bed made oration companye greate vehemence perswading exhorting manfully fight afterward saied terrible dreame slepe seming sawe horrible deuilles appere vnto hym pulling haling hym coulde take rest visyon fylled hym full feare also heuy care waked sore greued minde prognosticate dreame euill luke heuy chaunce came hym came cherful countenaunce vnto company wonte dooe leest thinke heauinesse feare enemy stoode vp rehersed vnto theim dreame thinke dreame rather conscience pricked sharpe stynge mischeuous offence although dooe pricke alwaye yet comenly wil byte moste towarde latter daye representyng vnto v onely selfe also terryble punyshement ordeined syghte deuill tearyng haling v therby haue grace may take occasyon bee penitet elles lacke dye desperacyon nowe come purpose nexte daye kyng richard hauing thynges redynesse went army oute tentes beganne sette men araye fyrst forward set forth meruelous lengthe bothe horseman also footemen veray terrible companye theim yt see theim farre formost parte ordered bowman stronge fortresse theim came ouer iohn ye duke norffolke hedde capitaine hym folowed kyng mightye sorte menne henry beyng departed ye communicacion frendes without tariyng pytched tentes nere enemy laye nighte comaunded men bee redinesse morninge sente also thomas standley middes betwixt bothe hostes come nere armye sent hym woorde set menne ordre tyll came answer otherwise thought mater dyd require alitel abashed stoode doubte yet yt taryed spede set menne ordre ye forward slender nouber fewe archer set formost parte ouer theim iohn earle oxford hedde capitain ryght wing sette gilbert talbot ye lefte put iohn sauage selfe ye helpe thomas standley folowed one companye horseman fewe footemen whole company scat fyue besides ye bothe stanley company willyam standley thre kinges army double bothe armyes redinesse beganne come within sight bragged forth theim selfes bothe party looking onely sygne token striking together betwyxte bothe hostes marresse whiche henrye lefte ryghte hande purposelye defence menne found meanes also haue bryght sunne backe myght dasyll eye enemyes kyng sawe henry passe ouer marras comaunded men violence set vpon theim sodein clamour lette arrowes flee theim syde paied theim home manfully came nere together laied valeauntly swerdes earle oxforde fearing least meane time kyng richardes multytude haue compassed menne whiche wer fewe comaunded theim fyues moue forwarde paste ten fote whiche comaundement knowen knitte theim selfes together seased fyghting aduersaries beyng afrayed suspected som crafte guyle began breake many parte wer much greued therwith wer glad ye king loste saued therfore fought lesse courage erle oxford menne thicke together stroke freshlyer parte dyd likwyse firste wardes batell fought manfully richard perceiued spy henry farre fewe companye armed menne afterward coming nere richard knewe hym sygnes token inflamed anger furiouslye stroke horse spurres ranne one syde hoste like lyon ranne hym syde henry perceiuing hym commyng desyrouse mete hym richard fyrste setting forth kylled diuers stode threwe doune henry banner willyam brandon bearer also ranne cheyny manne great mighte whiche came mete hym greate violece ouerthrewe hym grounde made hymself awaie theim come henry henry kept better tacke hym men would haue thought whiche allmoste despayre victory eue ye tyme lo came wyllyam stanley aide theim wt iii mene euen verie tyme residue kyng richardes men put flight richard fightyng alone middest enemy ouerthrowne slain ye meane tyme therle oxeford ye foreward fought mafully litle put ye residue flight slewe greate nobre agreate nombre whiche folowed richard feare loue helde xxii day moneth auguste inthe yere oure lorde thousand cccc lxxxvi ye conflict indured ii howres richard might fame went asaued hymself would afled awaie hym thei sawe menne begynnyng fight faintly ronne awaie vnto parte suspected treason willed hym flie mater manifest hope victory past thei brought hym swi te horse puttyng sied hope trust fleiyng made saied aunswere daie would haue ether ende battaill orels life suche greate audacite manfulnes whiche se certainly daie ob kyngdome quietely day life lose bothe euer entred emogest theim declared intendyng vtterly ether lose orels wynne wretehe dyed hauyng ende suche wont haue whiche stede lawe honestie godlynes folowe owne appetite vyllanye wyckednes plainly example whiche cannot expressed feare theim whiche suffer one howre bee multitude ye meane tyme one voyce one mynd proclaimed hym kyng whe thomas stanley sawe ye toke kyng richardes croune whiche founde emongest spoyle putte vpon head though created kyng eleccion people wonte bee olde tyme first token felicite kyng hery compaignie carriage went lecestre toward night bed whether refresshed compaignie well space twoo day thei might better goo toward london kyng richardes bodye brought naked ouer horse backe hed armes hagyng one side legges ye caried grey freres lecester surely myserable sight loke vpo yet good inough cosideryng wretched leuyng without solempnite buryed twoo dayes raygned twoo yeres twoo monethes one daie small stature hauyng deformed bodie ye one shoulder higher shorte face cruell looke whiche betoken malice guyle deceite muse vpo thing stading would byte vnder lippe continually whereby mane might perceiue cruell nature within wreched bodie striued chaffed alwaie hym self also dagger whiche bare aboute hym would alwaies bee
