suffered whiche called burning sweate sweating sickenesse intollerable men coulde kepe beddes lunatike person oute wittes ranne naked none almoste escaped ye wer infected therwith ye length great death many thousande menne learned presente remedye dysease yf sycke sweate daye streyghtelye downe clothes vesture yf nighte yt rise space xxiiii houres eate meate yf coulde forbeare drinke litle mighte disease reigned throughout england wherof also ensued plague token ye people iudged plaine argument kyng henrye shoulde neuer bee oute feare dreade mischaunce seing suche great vexacyon sedicyous tumulte rysen al claimynge crowne whe thynges wer apeaced london ordered owne mynd rode northward progresse pacifie realme especially partes firste commocion also wer priuie cloked frendes aduersaries nigh easter tooke waye lincolne tariyng certified lorde louell humfre stafforde gone sanctuary colchester place whether could tell whiche message kyng litle regardyng wet foorth apointed yorke came comocion made lord louell lorde stafforde shewed hym lorde louell hand strong power menne woulde inuade cytie also said lorde stafforde brother wer glocestre made insurreccion set menne euery parte defende gate walles citie first hearyng kyng litle moued certified letter frendes true greate feare neyther armye prepared harnyes theim mattier required haste least long taryeng aduersaries power might bee encreased multiplyed commaunded duke bedforde mete theim three thousande mene whiche harnysed barely theyr breste plate moste parte lether hym selfe yt meane tyme would gather vp hoste might euery place duke hauyng nigh ye tetes enemyes cosulted wt certain copaignie waye mighte traine theim peace withoute bloodde shedyng whiche deliberation aduisement decreed certaine shoulde proclaime openly yt thei haue pardonne woulde leaue battaile whiche proclamation auayled muche lorde louell eyther feare mystrust people feryng hym selfe owne behalfe fledde pryuely night compaignie lankeshire ther remained space syr thomas broghton knight hys army knowledge therof thei also submittyng theim selfes duke asked pardonne heinous offence lorde stafforde also hearyng great agony feare dyd take sanctuarye colname ii mile abindon sanetuary defence traytours taken place behedded brother doned thought haue done owne thorowe counsaill perswasion brother businesse asswaged yorke shyre set peace quietnes kyng went london shortelye wynchester quene wyfe deliuered prynce called arthure wynchester retourned agayne london sone chaunsed one syr richard symond preest borne nature traytour sedicious personne yet well learned chyld called lambert symenel bee hys scholar whome inuented crafte disceat woulde make chyld kyng england hym selfe archebyshoppe hygh potestate realme knewe verely many menne supposed kyng edwardes chyldren bee fled straunge place edwarde erle warwyke sonne duke clarence ether bee put death shortly ende myght ye better bryng hys purpose taught chyld bothe learnyng good maners also order hym selfe one linially descendyng hygh progenie sone rumoure younge earle warwyke dead prysonne preest heard intendyng therby bring matter aboute chaunged chyldes name called hym edwarde younge earle warwyke whiche boothe one age sayled irelande opening mynde certain nobilitee whome knew beare lytle fauoure kyng henry promysed ayde lorde gerardine chauncellour countree coulde dooe whyche lorde fyrst callyng hys frendes louers together desyred helpe restoryng yong earle herytage dyd sende certain englande desire theym kynge rychardes frendes continue loue faythfulnes towardes hym helpe hys nephiewes chylde ryghte hys power myghte bee stronger ouercome hys enemyes desyred lady margarete syster kynge edwarde wyfe duke burgondy hys purpose helpe whyche lady beyng flaunders promised messaungers would onely maintaine entente large mony substaunce laboure peynes myght occasion ye conspiracie kynge henrye certified thys sore greued meanes suche myscreaunte personne great sedicion bee neuerthelesse kynge consideringe shoulde bee destruccion manye menne yf shoulde fyghte enemy open feelde called hys counsayle together charter house besyde rychemounde consulted pacifie thys matter wythoute anye dysturbaunce fyrste decreed thei shoulde bee pardoned offence treason latelye commytted whiche hath frome tyme borne theim selfes vpryght towardes kinge leaste syr thomas broghton whyche kepte lord louell king great tyme wyth despeyring theyr pardon shoulde haue made sodaine insurrection agaynst hym men shoulde thyncke duke clarence englande appoynted shoulde showe hym selfe abrode wherby opynion ireland myghte bee frustrate accompted lye also determyned ladye elysabeth wyfe kyng edward iiii shoulde lose al landes submitted selfe doughters wholye handes kynge rychard contrary promyse made lordes noble whyche desyre lefte al englande fledde kynge henrye brytayne dyd sweare hym marye eldeste daughter wylled theim dooe purpose frame god would thys quene buylded collage cambrydge gaue landes maynteyning whiche thys houre called ye quenes collage thys order determynacion kynge ended wente london nexte sondaye folowynge caused young earle bee broughte tower streetes poules shewe hym selfe euerye bodye taske chiefe noble menne thoughte haue conspyred agaynste kynge henrye thys cause myghte perceaue iryshe menne moue battayle vnaduysedly cause stryfe vppon iuste occasion howebeit thys nothyng auayled earle lyncolne duke suffolkes soonne nephewe kynge edwarde coulde suffer kynge henrye thus reygne traytoure sayled flauders ladye margarete takynge wyth hym syr thomas broghton certayne also lorde louell landed twoo three dayes beynge together determyned earle lyncolne lorde louell shoulde goo irelande attend vpon counterfeyte earle brynge hym englande power myghte agaynste kynge henrye yf dooynges good successe foresayde lambarte misnamed earle shoulde consente counsayle deposed true earle bee delyuered oute pryson enherite right iuste tytle dominion kyng mistrusting man bee foolysh hardy fyght cause anye vndyscrete especiallye hys realme beleue dyd onelye mynde suppressynge iryshe menne theyr enterpryse subdue yet hearynge earle lyncolne fledde gooen hys aduersaries caused border bee dilygentlye kepte none myghte escape geue theym socoure commynge abbaye sayncte edmundes burye certified lorde thomas marque come excuse pourge hym selfe hym certayne thynges suspected whome kynge dyd sende earle oxford take commynge conueyghe hym towre london thys cause yf frende dede bee myscontented suffer lytle imprysonmente safetie hys kynge yf hys frende tarye myghte haue damage hurte hym kynge wente forthe norwyche tariynge christemas daye went walsingham thence cambridge streyght london tyme erle lincolne lord louell got two thousande germaynes wyth martyn swarte theyr captayne saylynge ireland came made fornamed lambarte kyng englande deuelynge wyth greate multitude iryshe menne aswell naked vnarmed personnes lorde gerardyne vnder hym sayled englande landed purpose wythin lytle lancastre trustynge bee ayded syr thomas broghton chiefe authoure thys conspiracie kynge slepynge hys mattiers mystrustynge thynges shoulde chaunce sente certayne knyghtes throughe easte party attende commynge hys enemyes gatherynge hys hooste together went hym selfe couentree beynge certified hym earle lyncolne landed lancastre wyth newe kynge whome kynge appoynted meete consente agremente hys counsayle goo vppon theym wythoute anye farther delaye least theyr power long sufferaunce bee augmented multiplyed suche aduisemente taken went notingham lytle woodde called boures pytched hys tentes whome shortelye came lorde talbote earle shrowesburye lorde straunge lorde cheiney wyth greate armye menne manye noble menne whose name ensue rauff longforde ihon montigomery henry vernone pek rauff shurley godfrey folgehan thomas gryfley edwarde sutton humfrey stanley humfrey staley wyllyam hugton wyllyam meryng edward stanope geruase clifton brian stapulton henry wylloughby wyllyam perpoyntes ihon babyngton wyllyam bedyll robert brundell ihon markham wyllyam merbury edwarde aborogh wyllyam tyrwite ihon hussey robert shefilde wyllyam newporte roger ormeston thomas tempest wyllyam knyuett henry wyllaybet lord edward hastyngges ihon dygby simo digby haringto richarde sachenerell ihon vyllers edwarde fyldyng thomas polteney nicholas vaux thomas gryne nicolas griffin edmund lucy edwarde belknap robert throgmarton george graie ruthin guide wolstone thomas fynderye dauid phillips thomas cheiney robert cotton ihon saint ihon ihon mordant thomas terell ihon raynsford robert paynton robert danyell henry marney edmunde aroundell also came fro ye ferdest partes realme noble men george oglye rauff neuill richard latemere wyllyam bulmere ihon langforde wyllyam norrys ihon neuill thortinbridge ihon wyllyams erle lyncolne meane season went forth softely compaignie yorkeshire without hurte discommoditie mane dwelt therabout trustyng partely therby tely also bycause well knowen acquainted emong theim get greate ayde socour perceiued none folowe hym could seyng enemy nigh hand also far entred safegard hoste returne bacward yet thought best abyde taste chaunce battaill muche yt rather sawe henry within twoo yeres accompaign ed fewe small sorte souldiers ouercome kyng richard whiche brought hym greate hoste well armed menne wherfore beeyng greate hope victory toke iorney then towarde newarke sette souldyours araye mete kyng knew well though bee paste ii dayes iorney hym could come thither kyng hery whiche surely certified thynges yt wet came newarke alitle euen thei fight yt morowe wyse erle loked tariyng long went forth three myles ferther sette tentes taryed night whose commyng although therle knewe yet went foorth lustely tourney came night village nigh enemy called stooke pitched tentes next daie kyng sone sette souldyours due ordre araye went forwarde wt spede place erle laye whiche place come appointed felde moste mete battaill bee fought gaue place enemy come foorth prouoked theim battaill ready prouoke readie wer thei owne courage come foorth bothe party thei ranne battaill fought moste egerly whiche flicte euidently appere germaines whiche sette forewarde whose capitain martine swarte nothyng woorse manlynesse cheualry thei gotte chiefly daily long exercise englishemen ireshmen although thei fought verie lustely yet reason thei ware harnes accordyng fasshio custome discomfcited beate downe bothe nobre soner yet battaill earnestlie boldly fought whyle bothe party could bee wel discerned whiche syde victorie would incline last kynges forewarde abode ieoperdie lustely couragiously ranne vpon enemy yt none hable resist abyde power yt aswell germaines irish men slain orels made flie ye whiche none could escape awaie whiche battaill whe thus dooen mene might se boldnes audacitie rebellios capitaines ihon erle lincolne fracis louell thomas broghto martine swart thomas gerardine neuer gaue backe one foote slaine place thei began first fight kylled vattaill fiue capitaines spoken euen partie foure thousand kynges part halfe theim whiche fought ye forewarde slain lambert child whiche falsly reported bee duke soonne clarece maister sir richard simond preest taken neither theim putte death lambert yet child seme dooe compulsion maister owne preest whiche defaulte cast perpetuall prisone lambert taken kynges kechin made one kynges faukeners yet lyue thus yt margarete went tyme turned naught none effecte whiche thyng whe heard tell flauders verie lory hearte made greate mone yet could bee contet immediately inueted thyng vexe trouble kyng henry shalbe shewed kyng henry thynges brought thus passe vtterly vanquisshed enemy thought hymself one tyme deliuered twoo eiuils together saie bothe feare present also come bee thought yt thei whiche fewe nombre durste bee bold entre realme make battaile ye kyng knewe wel ynough would bryng hym great well armed hooste felowes coniuracion whiche would mete ayde theim could tyme place conuenient therefore kyng sawe hoste enemy manifestly eye commaunded shoulde kyll earle lincolne bee brought hym alyue entent might shewe bewraye whiche ye conspiracie sowdyers would least sauyng hym bee destruccio haue dede many battayle fought yeare oure lorde thousande foure hundreth foure score secode yere heryes reigne ye whiche yere also thomas burscher archebyshop ca terburye died whose roume succeded iohn morton late bishop ely whome alexander name sixte bishop rome made cardinall retourne purpose kyng gathered al prayes spoyles together buryed theim wer slain went forth lincolne taryed three dayes euerye daie one procession thanke god almightie ouerhande enemy incontynently sent banner walsyngham consecrate lady bee kepte perpetuall mo ument victorie execucio suche rebellion taken shortely tooke iorneye foorth yorke likewyse suche founde gyltye dyd punyshe strayghtlye dooen wente vnto newcastle frome thence sente scotlande richarde foxe whiche longe made bishop exeter richarde edgecombe knight ambassadoures kynge iames league peace henrye thought great pleasure comoditee bee peace concorde kinges gouernours whiche laye aboute realme specially kyng iames yt rebellion might trust whiche otherwise perchaunce woulde haue trusted haue ayde succoure hande thereby durste none againe take weapon hym ambassadoures wer come scotland kyng hym gently moste louing fashion receiued heard dyd plainlye declare open theim yt hym selfe loued kyng henrye man yt moste parte scottes subiectes could case agree english menne wherfore excepte offend se theim desired ye legate bee contet truce vii yeres promesse dede sayed peace betwene theim parte shoulde neuer bee broken euer seuen yeres bee passed would geue truce seuen yeres lenger kyng henry would euer bee peace moste assured amytie kyng iames knewe facte people shoulde bee alowed ambassadoures hearde tooke yeres offered theim concernynge peace retourned home kyng ry againe shewed hym mattier ordre whiche tydynges veraye well contented shortely kyng departed thence towarde london waye leicetre mette hym abassadoures frenche kyng shewed hym kyng charles recouered many tounes cyties whiche possessed kyng maximilian kepte battayle nowe fraunces duke brytayne kepte socoured dominion certaine traytours rebellion hym whiche chief lewes duke orlyance therfore desyred hym frendship familiaritie either would helpe hym orelles medle neyther partie kynge henrye althoughe founde muche frendship frenche kynges hande yet muche spyed whereof stryfe beganne message well contente cause frenchemenne tooke battayle sawe duke olde manne neuer chylde thereby myghte brynge dukedome subieccion kyng henrye perceiued also howe louyng brytaynes euer englande finally remembred tendre loue betwene duke hym thought best nede wer helpe britaynes yet muche founde frenche kyng veray kynde tymes past partely helpe recouered kyngdome veraye lothe medle muche coulde well tell best mattier bee dooen laste fully purposed necessitie shoulde require helpe duke might yet least make highe frende hys extreme enemie aunswere ambassadoures intende make kyng duke frendes wherfore assone frenche kynges ambassadoures dimissed sent message christopher vrswycke charles kynge fraunce firste certifye hym veraye glad victorye vpon maximilian secondarely tumulte insurreccion made englad thyrdly especially desyre hym bee one againe duke brytayne commaunded vrswycke kyng fraunce shoulde bee contente go foorthe immediatlye duke desyre hym lykewyse kyng come againe london ioye myrthe victorye ye euery syde onely kyng also euerye one cytezyns reioysed veraye muche wherfore kyng shewed hym selfe beraye humane courteous toward menne also rewarded theim tooke paynes battaile moste bountefully long delyuered lord thomas marque oure loued hym veraye well meane season christofer vrswicke come frenche kyng hym louing fassion yt coulde bee receiued sone shewed message ye kyng shewed selfe bee wt veray well pleased went ye ambassadour streight thence comaunded hym britain shewed duke kyng henry would haue dooen duke hym self sicke great therby memory wit aied called hym heare message bothe lewes duke orleaunce councell whiche lewes wyse woulde haue peace bee made saied mete kyng henrye seing founde suche kyndnesse duke hande britaine suche good defence england helpe kepe battayle yt might frenchman retourned christofer againe fraunce declared king charles aunswer made ye britain shortely came englande againe still meane time ye frenche kyng went aboute busely ouercome brytains nigh purpose much ye exhorte desire kyng henry make peace betwene theim wherfore set bernarde daubeney knighte haste kyng henrye desire hym wise make ende co trauersy therupon kyng desirous chose thre oratours ye abbot abindon iohn lilie bishop rome collectoure richard tonshal knight veray wise man gooe firste frenche kyng duke make amitee frendshyp againe betwene theim euer ambassadoures proceded iourney iohn lilye fell sicke goute therfore hym chosen christofer vrswycke together wente comaunded firste fraunce kyng thence withoute delaye britain fraunces duke case would take suche condicyons wer offered wherfore came back againe fraunce without purpose tarieng signified kyng henry letter dooen letter came kynges handes edward woodilile bold champion came hym desired veraye earnestly myght haue host men helpe britain leasire cause dissencion betwene frenche kyng hym saied would gooe priuely without pasporte thentent might bee thought stole land kyng much trusted peace shoulde bee made woulde wyse graunt peticion wherfore edward wet streight ysle veches dominacion sone gathered menne together foure c sayled ouer britaines ioyned hym selfe theim frenchme whiche thing knowen fraunce made ye ambassadours greatly afraid liues while feare frechemen thought dooen maliciously kyng henry came ambassadours frome hym frenche kyng certifieng hym declaring euident toke nothing dede thought haue message albeit ye kyng lytle credece yet made thoughe bene angry ye ambassadours renewed peace betwene king hym xii monethes retourned home shewed kyng thinges yt either hearde sene wherof gathered ye frenchman nothing lesse entend haue peace made wherfore without delay called parliament consulted aidyng brytains exspence bee therin made mattiers assone parliament broken vp caused muster bee taken euery toune thorowoute realme yet leaste peraduenture might seme willingly breake amitee whiche betwene frenche kyng hym sent ambassadours fraunce certifye kyng late kepte parliament yt pleased noble sende helpe ye britain time dooen benefites englande nacios therfore either leaue battail orelles shoulde bee greued dyd obey ye mindes lordes prelate yet woulde promise hym one thing yt medle wt hym leger britain kepte battaile vpon theim commaundementes ye ambassadours went foorth declared ye french kyng minde wyll kyng thyng litle cared thought came passe dede englishemen coulde lytle auayle meane season britain fought one felde place called sainte albanes sped beray euel theim lewes duke orleauce many mo taken edwarde wooduile iames galeot italian veray good warryer diuers noble menne slaine whiche thing kyng henry heard tell thinking tyme make haste sente spedely roberte brooke lorde iohn cheinye iohn midelton raufe helton richarde corbet thomas leighto richard lacon edmond cornewell lustye capitaines viii thousand wel armed men ye brytains helpe theim theyr nede whiche reason ye wind serued theim came thither sone could desire frenche menne knewe comming whome knewe longe freshe lusty bee maner inuincible ye firste wer blanke durste scarsely looke oute tentes afterwarde trusting yt might wery theim went many theim together diuers place kepte many bikeringes english menne theim selfes euer bare worste away howsoeuer englishman sped sped naught while kynde warre exercise duke fraunces died dasshed chyefe ruler brytains theim corrupted money sturred vp ambicyon fell deuisyon amonge theim selues semed nomore endeuoure defende commune weale rather destroy vtterly extinguishe thing englishe menne perceiuing also suffering muche colde compelled necessitee within fyue moonethes wente thyther come backe agayne englande charles french kyng maried anne duke doughter gat al britayn meanes hys hades shalbe spoken decreed englande souldyours sent brytayne expence warre euery man paye thei hable tribute whyche mooste parte theim dwelte byshopryke durha yorke shyre dyd vtterly refuse pay complayned matter lorde earle northumberland immediately signified kyng letter people dyd greatly lament sory saiyng thei neuer put muche coast thei late dayes nowe ther much requyred theim neither thei hable pay great summe would pay yet al kyng comaunded erle get make theim pay whether thei would least peraduenture myght cause yf time tribute agayne bee required make insurreccion thyng people hearde ranne vnto earle authoure tribute paiyng themurde ryng erle northuberland kylled hym hande thei done thei chase ihon egremonknight verey dicious personne bee captayne arraied selfes went agaynst kyng makyng cry euery towne thei came fight nother cause defede yt comon libertie mattier shoulde come blowes thei waxed colde sorte theim euerye one wished tumulte wer retracted nowe alredy begonne coclusio one scacely scaped without great discommodite kynge assone hearde insurreccion went downe hoost yorke wherof slaues traitours beyng greatly afraied fledde hether thether durst abide sustaine power ye kynges army wherfore thei wer sone taken punished greuousely accordyng deseruyng euery one theim ihon egremont whiche captain fledde flanders margarete whome spake kyng sone busines que ched tooke iourny back vnto london committed tribute whiche yorke yorke bee taken vp holy richard toustal ye yere lord thousand foure hundred xc fourth yere reigne kyng henry thys yere also kynge scottes sore vexed subiectes roase agaynst hym made sonne iames whiche yet chylde capitain wherfore sent kynge englande frenche kyng byshoppe roome innocentius desire theim make end thys ciuile battayle contencion whiche betwene hys people hym whiche afterwarde sente theyr ambassadours desired vayne ye rude sort would nedes fight onlesse kyng scottes slain subiectes would resygne crowne wherfore shortely thei fought battayle kylled kyng gaue sonne iames whiche fourth name crowne byshoppe rome legate hadrian came late whyles englande wt kyng henry worde came kyng scottes slayne battayle hys soonne made kyng therfore taried england space veray muche made hyghly commended kyng ihon morto archbyshop canterburie whereby came high fauour kyng henry made bishoppe herforde shortly least gaue hym bishopprike boothe welles bathe longe retourned wt honour roome alexander made cardinall beganne also freshe certayne businesse concernynge brytaine geare appeased whiche maximilian beyng tyme without wyfe would haue maried duke briteines doughter one wowed hym lady promisyng hym fayth trueth entent might go word vsed way wt went bed night bedde wedlocke wower hired putte one fete ye bed knee ye sight copany many noble matros lady token testimony yt mariage consumate thei ii wife nothing auaile char frenche kyng desireous marye hearyng maximilia sure dyd busely set vpon britaynes thentent might haue ladye countree also wyll estemed mariage bee strength force neuerthelesse feared kyng henry muche least would stoppe purpose whiche kyng made league ferdinande also kyng spayne made ye britaynes assist theim ieoperdies perilles chaunce theim foren countrees wherfore sent al post hast francese lucemburgense charles marignane roberte gaguine kyng henry peace bee confirmed hadde desyrynge hym kyng might ordre mariage ladye anne wer thought best without let hynderaunce hym kyng henry would agree theim lady bee maried hym consyderyng made sure kyng maximilian right lawe bothe god manne albeit kynge would gladly make peace betwene theim bothe demissyng ye kynges ambassadoures large ample rewarde sent thomas goldestone abbot cantorbury lord thomas ormondye ambassadours streight theim meane space alexander b rome sixt name innocetius sent bishop cocordiense legate frenche kyng certayne mattiers emong peace vnitee bee confederate betwyxt hym kyng henry whiche easely obteyned came englande beyng entretained moste roially kyng purpose desire hym englishe ambassadours beyng frenche kyng purposed haue peace concluded whiche first demaunded certain thynges kyng ere bee made albeit kyng would graut theim nothyng sore moued request askyng ye shortly frenche kyng sent noble menne britain greate giftes rewardes entent thei might moue ladie anne giue troweth hym also sent many princely giftes token ye would beare loue hym yt might feare might lawfully marie hym certified ye promise none effecte yt gyue maximilia yt geue made wtout cosent whiche ye gouernaunce dominion ouer ye countre cause concorde peace could bee kept betwixt theim kyng taken maximilians doughter ladie margaret bee wife saied might bee lawfully dissolued ye ladie vnder age ripe bee maried ladie anne britain persuasion many noble menne countree contented bee wife ladie kyng certified hastened mariage expedicion celeritee could englishe ambassadours returned countree nothyng dooen agreed vpon matter kyng certified ambassadours purposed make battaill hym reuenge naughtie entent swerde assemblyng counsaill together showed theim matter iuste cause fight desteryng theim maintenaunce thesame warres helpe hym money neuerthelesse menne thynke bee extorte theim willed euery mane gyue muche litle would theim bee estemed taken moste beste assured frendes gaue ye money somme gatheryng preparaunce made battaill maximilian kyng warred sore frenchemen whiche kyng taken litle certain brunt skirmishe made cast prisone whiche tyme kyng henry sent hym giles dabeney capitain calais aide hym three thousad harnissed mene ye length maximilian hauyng better hand frenchemen enteded reuenge hymself freche kyng repudiate doughter ladie margarete taken hym wife quene anne fully hable hymself sustein battaill sent iames conti alde ambassadour kyng henry helpe whiche iames dooen message kyng promised would dooe hym could mainteinyng warres tyme charles frenche kyng maried ladye anne chalengyng mariage dominion gouernaunce ye brytaines maximilian kyng beyng certified greately moued onely forsake repudiate doughter ladye magarete also receiued mariage ye ladye quene anne wife furie sent kyng hery desieryng hym prepare armie would goo vpon frenche menne kepe open battaill theim whiche kyng henry gathered hoste menne proclaimed battaill realme whiche proclamacion came london houge armie menne capitaines whiche herafter ensewe folowe rycharde thomas greate compaignie welshe menne erle thomas derbie george erle shrowesburie thomas erle harundell edmunde duke suffolke edwarde erle deuenshire wt noble young soone thomas erle ormo dye george erle kent lorde thomas dorcet marque ihon cheyney gyles dabeney richard gylforde ihon raynsforth iames terell ihon sauage thomas baro helto wyllyam bulmerey edwarde stanley armie araied kyng sent sir christopher vrswycke sir ihon ryseley knyghtes kyng maximilian certifye hym thei redynesse kepe battaile would haue theim dooen message thei returned backe kyng certifiyng hym maximilia poore nedye monye menne could hable susteyne battaile neuerthelesse mynde good power habilitee correspondent kyng receipte letter displeased muche hym albeit consyderyng gooen farre suche furnyture thynges prepared least menne shoulde impute hym cowardnesse faynt fro battaile proceded forth towarde fraunce ye vi daye septebre landed calise rested armye wher worde brought hoste thei knowe maximilian could make preparaunce lacke mony ye whiche thei maruailed greatly consideryng suche vilanye shewed hym longe kynge fraunce hand yet thei wer neuer discoumfeyted like stoute valiaunt warryars great confidence owne power strengthe wyth kyng fraunce yt perceaued best profite ease would gladly haue reconciled although ready hoste fight theim withstade power especially desyred peace cause yt might haue loue neighboures entent realme might bee better sauegarde quietnes whe warre ferdinad kyng napels ye desyre ludouike sfortia duke millayn whiche present tyme inuite hym wherfore sende philip desquerd chief annonye desyre kyng henrye peace whiche philip send ye letter hym came countre hymself wherin signified would take suche paine bryngyng purpose would please grace reconcile bothe hym kyng loue eche thei haue dooen heretofore saied bee honour take thesame condicion whiche condicion would send certain capitains mete hym parte fraunce determine haue promised hereafter duely bee performed kyng red letter send bishop exceter giles dabeney forenamed philip peace agreed vpon concluded whiche space determyned vpon certain condicions whiche shalbee shewed peace bee bothe party thei thus consultyng ye kyng hauyng hoste caleis remoued place bononye pitchyng tetes beseeged toune power might whiche toune strongely defended furnished thynges necessarye warre could bee ouercome without greate labour yt either could ouercome parte woord brought peace cocluded made whiche heard pleasure frenchemen sorowe englishe men thei cried kyng saied honour dooe kyng wise manne moste prudent prince saied death many noble puisaunt capitaines continue thesame battaill therefore might sore reproche wer power tendre well health comons owne whiche saiyng somewhat coule pacifye grief dooen kyng returned backe calise enformed hym yt one richard ye named hym self ye sonne kyng edwarde made insurreccion flauders ye counsaill lady margarete ye quene fight hym thyng kyng henry consyderyng spedely hasten conclude peace condicion peace bee made yt frenche kyng paye kyng henry certain summe meny whiche leauyed ambassadours cost charge kyng put battayll also yerely certain space paye cause bee payde kyng englad full recompence x v thousand crounes whiche frenche kyng beyng warre italian payd said tribute ye noble prince souereigne lorde kyng herye v sonne henry seuenth full reco cion frendship bee euer yere lorde thousand foure hundreth foure score thirtene seueth yere reigne also inuadyng besiegyng bonony whiche spake none killed sauyng onely syr ihon sauage whiche goyng tent wt syr iho riseley taken priuely rydyng walles ye toune would yelde slain frenche men albeit syr ihon rysely fled escaped daunger kyng went fro cali england yet might wtout trouble busynes quene margaret spaine whiche euer watched hym displeasure perceauyng yt erle copaignie could haue suche successe businesse would haue wished theim inueted new way worke treason certain youg tornace beautiful faire coutenaunce pregnaunt witte whiche youg called peter surnamed warbecke cowardnes nycknamed englishe men called perkyn perkyn warbeck youg trauaylyng many countrees could speake many laguages basenes stocke birth knowen none almost therfore ye quene thynkyng youg man bee mete might feigne duke yorke sone brother kyng edward kept hym certain tyme wt priuely tellyng hym yt might rather persuade kynges sonne send hym irelade time knewe kyng henry apointed fight frenche kyng honorably receaued taken euery manne prynce whose right promysed fight helpe hym yt could came ye freche kynges eare yt one ireland kyng send see caused hym brought came psence ye kyng accepted hym gladly princely fashio intreteined hym ye came loue wt kyng england sayd charles dimisse ye youg would loger kepe hym least inconueniencie cause strife chaunce thorough wherfore ye young manne went flaunders agayne quene magarete whiche quene receaue hym suche gladnesse coulde well rule selfe cause onely dyd shewe selfe ioyfull merye menne mighte perswade theim selfe richard kynges soonne vpon cause truely men ye reuerence younge manne yt firmely beleue hym bee righte heire sonne kyng edwarde also rumour blased abrode aswel england fraunce flaundres beganne great sedicion spryng firste long sanctuary greate offence commytted wer cast pouertie gathered compaignie sayled ouer flaunders counterfaicte edwarde otherwise named peter also many noble men conspired together entent might bryng purpose wel send certain quene margarete knowe thesame edwarde might come conueniently englande ye thei beyng certified thesame might ye easely receaue bryng hym ye realme yt consent agrement theim syr robert clyfforde knight wyllyam barley wer sent shewe myndes aduyce concernyng newe founde duke quene margarete whome quene accepte gladlye persuaded theim true publyshed rycharde duke streight vpon shewed theim thesame peter whiche muche lyke richarde praysyng vertues qualitees wonderfullye said robert whe seen thesame youg manne beleued surely kynges bloode wrote englande coumpaignye felowes conspiracie knewe hym bee kynges soonne face euery proporcion body letter came vnto englande chief capitaynes businesse openly diuulgate publyshe trewe spoken saied abroad duke dooen suche crafte manne coulde tell authoure rumoure kyng perceiued many men geue credence vaine fable thought beste owne safegard prouide remedy also mystrusting conspiracye bene made bicause sir robert clifford fled priuely flaundres commaunded certain knightes chosen piked menne warre wt bonde menne kepe border surely ye manne might escape sayle ouer sea without pasporte licence geuen hym also men myghte contynue false perswasion belefe conceyued duke caused certain spy search citees belgike knowe progenie mysnamed richarde geue theim highe rewardes would shewe verite truth matter sailynge fraunce euerye manne dyd gooe contraye quarter enquired diligently hym ye length certain theim came towne called tornace certifyed testymonye many honest menne came lowe course parentage named peter war becke whiche thing also kynges frendes certified hym letter writynges hym plaine euidentelye therfore kyng knowen matter wholy aswel frendes spy sent foorth purposelye caused bee proclaimed openly aswell region countrees england disceate deuelish crafte might appere euident euery manne firste sent ambassadours philyp chiefe capitaine flaundres councell younge age whiche sir edward poninges knight sir william varame preest lawyer might shewe euidently howe falsely younge manne hath vsurped name richarde duke yorke whiche kylled brother edward towre london comaundement kyng richard vncle euery man coulde testifye affirme surely also borne poore stocke obscure famulie tornace named perkin warbecke therfore woulde please hym councel suffer theim selfes bee blynded seduced suche mere imposture craftie illusion yet aide hym hande cause sedicion strife consideryng iuste title enheritynge would rather bee frendes nowe yt helped maximilian theyr kyng yere againste power violencye frenche menne hym selfe hable refyste theyr myghte stronge power ambassadours dooen message gentely entretayned hym request woulde loue oughte vnto kynge counsaile helpe thesame perkin thinge neuerthelesse yf quene margaret would persiste continewe malice towardes kyng whome ambassadour sir william varame reproued checked sore bringing vp suche monster commune plague publike weale oration made vnto philippe counsayle power withstande might doo owne herytage thinges owne wyll pleasure whiche quene entended fully arme perkin stronge compaignye menne kyng henry kynge henrye dyd heare purposed pacyfye busynesse like chaunce wytte policye streight dyd sende foorthe certaine spy whiche shoulde fayne theim selfes haue fledde vnto duke meanes searche foorthe knowe whole entente theyr coniuracion waye framed theyr matter also shoulde promyse pardon remyssyon vnto syr roberte clyfforde willyam barley offence comitted kyng dooen many theim returned englande broughte name certayne chief conspiracye taried vntyll suche tyme sir robert clifforde came englande agayne kyng knowen chief capitaines tumulte spyes theim caused bee attached brought london presece whose name wer sir iohn ratclyffe syr simon monforde syr thomas thwarte knightes william dabeney roberte ratcliffe richard lesey wt many also certaine preestes religious menne sir william richeford thomas poynes bothe monkes sainct dominikes order sir william sutton sir william vrseley deane poules robert layborne giltie crime hearing many compaignie wer taken fledde take sanctuarye taken wer condempned treason ye whiche heded sir simon monford sir robert ratcliffe william dabeney authours chiefe capitaines busines pardoned preestes also order taken also sir iohn ratcliffe pardoned lyfe came calisse caste prisone behedded corrupted kepers wt many promise haue escaped shortly sir robert clifford trusting find fauour grace kynges hande came england whose coming ye kyng certified went streight ye towre london taryed tyll suche tyme ye syr robert clyfford came whiche thyng vsed vnder pretence yf sir robert clifford accused man hym ye treason euerie suche person mighte bee called thether withoute anye suspectio anie euel streight bee cast holde goo furder wyll shewe opinion many men conceaued knightes goynge flaunders men helde opinion kyng henrye dyd sende hym spye flaunders therfore came soner fauoure neuerthelesse lyke bee true diuerse reasos fyrst tourned ye great infamye hurt hym selfe frendes secondarly greate fauoure kyng ben tymes past giltie part therfore saied sir robert comming king retourne england kneled mekelye downe foot desired pardo grace beyng enquired coniuration examined wer authours mischiefe pronounced saied william sta ly whome kynge made earle one chief saied kyng greatly dismayed greued offend made chief priuie chamber considering also founde great kindenes hertofore hande dyd ouercome kyng rychard chiefly helpe meanes kyng coulde bee perswaded suche offender bene shewed manifest token apparet argumentes ye true saied king caused taken examined matter examinacion proued offender kynge doubtynge dooe dyd consult breath lytle selfe feared brother lord thomas shewed great kyndnesse woulde take greuously also yf shoulde remitte faulte would abuse lemtee trespace highly albe laste wylled shoulde suffer offence caused hym bee behedded cause loue reporte dyd chaunge hatred lorde wyllia consideryng saued kyng brought hym realme gouernour thought could neuer bee recompensed hys doyng wher kyng also remembring benefyte dyd make hym chiefe chamberlayn gaue hym hyghest promocions lytle regarded loked greater rewarde wherfore king perceauynge sore greued hym thei bothe dyd fall debate hatred eche wyth also time king thought best vse asperite correcting offeces subiectes ye taken suche heart audacitee ye thei feared speake euel maiestie spiteful contumeleous wordes trusting euer ye fayned rychard duke york lately rysen death lyfe god name claime crowne enheret counterfeted father possession persos suffered due ponishment offence learning neighbour mischaunce beware dyd frome ye tyme beare theim selfes true faithfull subiectes assysted al power time required help death william stanley giles dabeney chosen made chiefe cha berlain ye kyng good staye realme sauyng yt ireland wel weded pernicious sede ye sowed young perkin warbeck secte wherfore sent sir henry deny late abbot lankto abbey thither made chauncellour ouer al ile edward ponyng serch place forenamed perken punish extremely example ye giltie yt crime thei heard thei fled part woddes marysh place defence safgard selfes consultyng kepe open warre agaynst hym whiche edwarde persued theim many time coulde neuer try wyth thei wer disparsed foren wilde people returned backe suspectinge earle kyldare occasion attached counsayl erle euel willers brought prisoner england wher arained certain matter treason laied charge aduoided clerly quite selfe whome kynge dimissed sente hym irelande bee gouernour captayne ouer theim kyng beeyng oute feare battayle dyd take hys progresse shyre recreate spirites solace selfe mother lady margarete wyfe countesse earle darby yet ye king thus delityng hym selfe perken warbecke could moderate rule hym selfe although manye suffered put execucion mischife proue chaunce battel gathered great armye men aswell prisoner slaues sanctuary men came kent wind serued ther caused certayne land enquire yf ye kentish men would bear kentish working guile promised ye thei would assist yf co panie would land ther albeit perke fearing ye thei meaned falshode craft would descende selfe caused certain souldiours lande whiche persones beynge pretye way shippes wer sore beate put flight many theim taken prisoner wer condempned dye wherfore perke failing purpose fled backe flaunders consulted frendes vntyll suche time better prepared bothe men counsayle kynge herynge hys enemyes made etrauce realme left progresse purposed go london beynge certified next day wel thei sped continued went forth progresse sendyng theim richard gilford geue thankes promise good turne herafter ye good seruice thei done tumultes assaultes enemy also thei might haue accesse herafter party king commau ded ye lordes bee defeded strogely wt bulwarkes sure munimetes fortress whiche perken beyng certified hastened ye renue battaill kyng yt might haue longer space delaye dooe thynges defence realme came irelande armie tariyng space sailed scotlande ayde succour kyng iames trustyng finde grace hand spake maner thinke vnknowe moste noble kyng ruine stocke edwarde fourth name late whiche dooe know please grace take soonne power god preserued liue houre mightie hand tiranne father died apointed brother richard duke gloucestre bee gouernour tectour albeit rather destroyer progenie mainteiner wyllyng kyng hymself depriue v right title commaunded bothe bee slain dispatched worlde therfore hauyng full power ordre v cause brother bee destroyed yt might bee without parte offense shewe hymself tirane caused bee conueighed straunge foren countree bee desolate comforte helpe kyng richard hold croue dispatchyng away v two could tell reason tendre age vntill late myne aunte ladie margarete beyng flauders shewe seen entent might recouer father possession hath geuen power bonde mene wyllyng ye desire helpe externe nacions countrees come succoure reported helpe tymes euery manne right case bee shall finde fauorable shall binde myne neuer thynke ourselfes hable make amendes thus saied kyng promised hym neuer repente hym commyng hym bad take good hearte kyng assemblyng counsaill together asked thei thought best matter whether deliberacion bee take theim w sest aunswered folishenes go fur suche matter consideryng painted feigned duke right england also saied diuerse cause moste profitable comen wealth partely parkyn matter goo well forwarde would rewarde theim thei would desire enriche realme moste plentefully liberalite partely also henry kyng perceiuyng kyng assist hym would gladly paie tribute hym peace concord bee counsaill gyuen kyng gladly folowe loue might bee apparent people caused ladie katherine doughter therle hutley nigh kinsema maried hym dooen kyng willyng yt perkyn reigne englade hastened iourney towarde border comyng proclamed openly ye bee pardoned ye would beare duke yorke fight quarell mene might feare submitte theim selfes thei burned spoyled killed wt mercie ferre thei go kyng perceiuyng yt englishemen came aide young duke souldiours wer loden wt praies spoiles yt thei would gladly go returned backe scotlad cariyng wt hym infinite goodes rich duke came scotlande consideryng greate distruccion losse englishman none came aide hym entet iuglyng countrefeict dignite might perceiued saied verie craftely loude voice oh wretch stonie hearte moued losse death many englishemen myne woorde desired kyng yt would molestate realme herafter suche cruel tormentyng fieryng kyng shaped hym aunswere right shortely truely sir thynke take charge thought mannes realme owne coulde se manne woulde take parte helpe power whe last emong theim cause ye kyng litle esteme hym tyme countyng hym incostant vnstable speakyng woordes agreyng promise ye english lordes captaines hearde busines thei wer greate feare fled safegade life euery manne castell holde gatheryng axmie withstand enemy certified kyng post haste scottes enterprise whiche hearyng prepared armie hast fight theim scottes beyng lode praies spoiles thei gone backe countre ere englishe menne could bee readie first commocion busines scottes englishemen scottes thus gone kyng certified thought suffer theim lenger leste long tariyng deferryng ye matter thei take heart fearsenes inuade realme assemblyng counsaill together shewed theim proffite publique weale warre enemy thei agreed right gladly mainteinyng battaill leuyed certain summe tribute paid euery mannes hed whiche paiment although easie small yet many commen people grudged paie parliament also conuocacion certain lawes actes statute confirmed made thought moste expediet publique weale dooen kyng prepared fight haste gatheryng armie made giles dabeney graund capitain ouer theim goyng scotlande beganne sodenly ciuile battaill realme whiche paiment money ye cornishemen whiche made insurreccion beeyng poore could well paie tribute gatheryng together one michael ioseph smyth thomas flamoke take blacke smyth vpon theim gouernaunce compainie seyng theim greued sore paye muche incense theyr myndes againste prynce albeit layde faulte cause exaction ihon morto bishoppe catorbury ruigenald braye chief kynges house thus preparyng theim selues warre whe aswell sufficiente viandrye thynges ready tooke theyr iourney welles thence entended go london kyng shewed auditours wer vp lorde twychet lorde audely nobylitee taken partes thought fyrste scoure realme suche rebelles traytours ere would fight scottes therfore caused giles dabeney returne backe agayn goyng vpon scottes whose armye encreased multiplyed many pycked freshe warryers might better lesse laboure ouercome rebelles also least scottes might nowe hauyng good oportunite inuade realme time ciuile battyle caused lorde thomas erle surrey puissaunt redoubted warryer whome taken prysoner ouerthrowe kyng richard litle set libertie made treasourer englade death iohn dynham gather bond men durham kepe ye scottes yf chaunce come vntyll suche tyme yt cornyshe menne beyng pacified subdued might send theim forenamed giles agayne power armye noble hearde busynes came london euery many could make ayde kyng yf nede shoulde compaignie erle essex lorde mongey erle suffolke richard thomas william say lorde haward erle surrey sonne noble young man stoute courage robert lytton thomas bande robert clyfforde wyllyam dauers george verye thomas terell richard fizlewes ihon baynsforth thomas brian richard poole thomas harecourte ihon hampden edward barkeley willya bolongue sonne thomas henry haydon robert clarence philip calthorpe robert louell ihon shaye thomas frouwike many lower degree certayn nobilitie mete theim commyng kepe theim purposely douer vntyll suche tyme busynesse ended might knowe wise nowe cornyshemenne gooynge welles theyr graunde capitayne lorde audeley went saulisbury fro thence wynchester kent looked helpe deceaued earle kent lorde burgone poole lorde cobham thomas burcher edwarde ponyng richard gilforde wyllyam scotte iames cromer ihon peche iohn darel henry wyat rychard haulte ihon fogge ready withstande theyr power cause people beare trewe heartes theyr kynge whiche many cornyshe men faynted lesse mynde fight feare fled priuely nyght compaignie captaynes perceauyng coulde haue helpe theyr handes trusted theyr owne power brought theim blackeheath feld nigh london pytched theyr tentes playn byd battail kyng would mete theim el inuade cytie whome kynge perceauyng readye fight caused henry burschere erle essex edmunde polam erle suffolke richard thomas three noble warryers besiege theim sydes wyth two wynges came hym self myddest sendyng giles dabeney greate power commyng thus felde bothe erles richard thomas sette vpon theim violently first brunt put theim flight killed aboute two thousande re sied tooke prisoner could bee told emonges theim ye captaynes shortely wer put death michael ioseph suche stoute courage valiautnesse yt neuer fainted gaue backe vntyll tyme stryken downe kylled openly battaile ended kynge loste thre hundreth compaignye wer kylled presente also prysoners taken pardoned sauyng captaynes first autours mischief whose quarter would haue bee put stake set dyuerse place cornewell theyr naughtie dooynges foolishe entrepryses might bee document hereafter beware many coutree would gladly haue renewed battaile yf might haue capitayn yt wer nothyng abashed ye ouerthrowe theyr late insurreccion turned mynd yt thei wer thither quarter set vpo stake whe busines ye kyng scottes certified certain spy thought best inuade englande againe burned waye lest kyng prouoke hym force dooen muche hurte thus came durham burned aboute entending also wynne norham castle whiche bishoppe furnished litle menne vitaile sufficiently coulde haue none accesse castell bishop foxe bishop exeter godlines verteouse liuing continue euer henrye entreated hartelye king scottes peace hope wrote vnto kyng englande would please hym sende one noble helpe conclude matter hym scottes kyng greate trouble veraye desierous peace sent byshoppe durham hym haste henrye bishop reasoned scottyshe ambassadours concernyng peace albeit thei could agree kyng henrye desiered haue perkyn warbecke cause busynes greatly disquieted realme whome kyng woulde delyuer although might ryghte consideryng falsehode deceyte vsed hym therfore reasoned much matter could bring ende yet truce taken certain yeres condicion perkin warbecke bee conueyghed oute scotland tary longer whyle dooinge kyng henry caused ambassadours ye frenche kyng bee brought hym shewed wer stopped douer iourney vntill suche tyme yt insurreccion eornish men ceassed hearing yt came peace league bee made grauted theim right gladly yt nowe beig reconciled wt ii kynges thesame neighbour thanked fernand wife elizabeth ye caused peace bee made betwixte hym scottes rewarded ambassadoure moste worthely princely maner tyme vnitee concorde made yere oure lorde thousande foure hundreth foure score eighten ye xii yere kyng henry reigne kynge scottes kepte promesse xii pere ry vii well ynoughe perceiued manifestly deluded called vnto hym perkin warbeck first declared benefites pleasure dooen vnto hym counsailed hym gette hym vnto place mighte byde safegarde come againe another time shoulde haue oportunitee neuer looke helpe partely made peace kyng englande partely sawe englishemen came take parte wherfore desired hym bee misgreued thus leaue hym also counsailed hym goo place regyon wherfore perkin veraye sorye kyng counsailed hym departed thence wife went ireland determining hym selfe might haue helpe menne cornewale retourne thence faste myghte bee home greate mailres aunte margaret flaundres soner come thither heard diuers messenger yt cornewale ready fyght kyng henry euer wer hoope whiche went streyght cornewall dyd sturre vp heartes gyftes promyses immediatelye called capitain saied thei woulde folow hym thinges obey promptly hys commaundementes perke good hoope euer would nothynge rashelye withoute aduisemente purposed fyrste ouercome citees wel defeded place lay way get many coulde folowe hym take part incontinently buckle ye kynges host whe thus deliberate wet streight exeter next citee coulde come vnto besieged gunnes breake downe walles laboured myght bee breake gate saw thei could easely betten downe thyng streight set fyre theim whereof citezins veray sore afraied priuely night let downe diuerse ouer ye walles rope go certifie kyng trouble meane tyme whe thei saw enemy almost bret vp gate one side tooke great blockes set fyre side none cause aswell enemyes therby might excluded thei selfes included thei trusting made also wtin great ditch thi ge defend inuasio rebelles perke saw got ladder would meanes haue come citee came sone vp thei beate downe meanes many slayne thet would thence depart trusted surely laste thei glad yelde theim selfes al wer within lack viandrie sone kyng hearde hasted hoost toward exeter faste possible sente dyuerse souldiours beefore certifie menne commyng preparaunce tyme set forth helpe theym exeter thomas trencherd william corteney walter cortney edmond carre ihon halemel peter eggecomb thomas fulford iho crook william saintmaur great host whose capitain edward corteny erle denshire sonne william whiche young man mooste noble courage whiche thyng peter heard tell left besiegyng exeter went ye nexte towne whiche called tautun vieued hoost set aray redye fyght howbeit lytle affiaunce many souldiours slenderly harneissed better skylled warre kyng sawe gone tautun hasted thither spede thether came also edward ye duke buckingham young veray valiaunt lustie courage hym folowed greate compaignye noble men giles brigge alexander brayha moryshe barkeley robert tame ihon sapcot ihon wadha hugh lutrel nycholas hys sonne william orton thomas lynde ihon semar wylliam norris thomas blunt ihon guyse roberte poynte harry vernon ihon mortimer ihon speke rychard beaucap fraunces chenie roger tokete roger wenburg henry roger edwarde darell ihon langforde richard lacon thomas tremaile edwarde sutton amis paulet ihon byknell wyllyam sayntemaur thomas longe nycholas latimer ihon turbaruyll wylliam martyne walter hungorforde moryshe baron rycharde corbet thomas cornuall many besydes king came nygh towne sente begynne battayle roberte broke lorde rycharde thomas giles dabeney great stronge hoost entent hym selfe souldiours myght set vpon behynd deuise purpose kyng al superfluous perkin sone espyed kyng redie fight fledde priuely nyght sanctuary bellylo abbey lurked whether perke dyd feare least men forsake hym timeditie hym selfe much vncertayne probable sure kyng tooke hys flyght greate commoditee corneshe menne surelye purposed eyther wynne ouercome theyr enemy elles one theim haue lyued anye daye lenger kynge henrye knewe perkin gone sente hym many horse menne yf myghte bee shoulde ouertake hym hys iourney brynge hym backe perkyn warbecke made suche spede seene came sanctuarie petie capitaines coulde scape clene theim moost part ta ken brought backe againe kyng residue souldiours thei vnderstode ye perkyn chief capitain fled ye taken gaue vp theim selfes king without busines hym gently wer forgeuen dooen kynge went ereter gaue great thankes wer worthy punished authoures sturrers vp insurrection moost straitlye ye meane tyme many souldiours road mighels mounte chaunce found katherin perking wife brought streight like bond woman captiue kyng kyng sent accompanied goodly sort matron goodly young woman london quene true sure token vyctorie while taried exeter supposyng selfe could haue perfect victory vntyl gotte perkin self beginner sedicion strife sent forth two company menne besiege sanctuarye wher perkin meanes myght scape away sent worde also certain trustie messenger yf would humblie submit selfe forgeuen committed wherfore perkin seynge ponderynge state miserie wet voluntarily sanctuary commytted hym selfe kynges pleasure kyng weray glad toke iourney immediatly towarde london without great metyng people whych came euery quarter se feloe monstre beyng aliente durst bee bold come noble realme make battaill delude noble menne suche fassion whe kyng come london appointed certain menne kepe hym bothe night daie verie vigilantly thentent might neither conueigh hymself lande ner goo whether within realme make like perturbacion disquietnes kyng perceiuyng ye many well somerset deueshire whiche helper rebelles greatly bothe goyng foorth commyng homeward thought good punishe theim also least peraduenture thei might ye bold dooe like thyng therfore committed busines amis paulet knight robert sherburne deane poules dooen serchyng suche thoroweout bothe shire wer verie exacte diligent thei wer fauorable al feare compulsion yet thei none fauorable thei thought defaultes indifferently punished equitie therin verie well executed yere small matter befell greate strife betwene kyng henry iames kyng scotlande whiche strife beganne fassion certain younge menne ye scottes came armed vnto duresme castell beheld wonderous circumspectly though thei desierous know dooen whe kepers castle could perceaue yt thei went aboute hurte displeasure seing theim go awaie owne accorde thei made woordes let theim alone thei came nexte daie vieued likewise kepers ye said castel demaunded theim intent thei auswered theim like rude vnmanerlie ientlemenne frowardly could bee thought muche yt laste muche altercacion bothe party thei fell together eares scottes slain residue put flight whe thei came home certified kyng thesame wherwith beyng sore moued angre set woorde kyng henry would wtout doubt reuenge querell wherfore kyng hery verie sorie much forfeare liue quietnes peace age made auswere yt doe default cousaill rather rashenesse subiectes whiche thei could bee ued guiltie accordyng faulte punished wherfore desired moste louingly coteted hable mitigate swage scottes angre outrageousnesse whiche cause richard bishop duresme whiche heuie seruuates ye beginner discord wrote many letter kyng iames desire hym kepe peace bee quiet whiche letter kynges rage quenched yt bothe sent verie kynd letter hym desired hym hartely come ouer talke hym ye whiche tydynges bishop verie glad went streight kyng henry shewe hym matter leaue hym incontinenly go ouer hym came scotlade receiued louyngly coulde bee thought kyng hymself abbey called melrose complained muche crueltie vsed toward menne englade beganne commen secretly matter especially amitie betwene kyng henry hym whiche bee euer stablished confirmed desired yt kinges doughter margaret mariage whiche thyng albeit bishop glad heart yet would make perfect aunswere sheweforth sure hope ye saied came home would dooe best matter laie hym wherfore kyng shortly dimissed hym desired hym ernestly breake ye matter kyng hery whe come home ye proffer pleased ye kyng verie well manne whiche alwaies delited wt peace quietnes wt troublesomnesse battaill approch ye death perkin warbeck edwarde erle warwicke whiche long lyen readie tower perke thought would saue hymself therfore tyme tooke leggues ranne awaie sone kyng harde tell therof made menne hym spede ye might bee wt whose clamour shoutes perkyn feared yt necessitie compelled go abbaie called bethele ther intreacted ye abbot place desire kyng pardon might dye whiche thyng abbot hym obteined wherfore perken brought bounde feitered westminster stoode whole daie sight menne great shame reproche hym self partely kyng promised hym life partely renne awaie comitted ye towre wickednes boylong hote within breit would suffre hym escape vegeauce punishemet god shortly moste iustly worthely put deathe herafter shalbe shewed chaunsed ye monke whose name patricke scholer whome promised would folowe counsaill easely come kyngdome englande whiche scholer one heard maisters mynd verie instaunte matter desired maister forget purpose rather begynne sone possible wherfore thei twene theim selfes taken deliberacion counsailled thyng brought passe thei went bothe together kent beganne young feloe tell priuely many erle warwicke gotte tower helpe monke whiche perceiued credence geuen declared openly desyred al men helpe euer sedicion beganne goo foreward heddes principalles thesame wer taken casle prysone whiche one condempned death condepned perpetuall pryson darkenesse tyme englande muche attrybuted prestes al religious though committed felonie murder yea treason haue bene therfore condempned death moreouer whosoeuer could reade though wer neuer lytle crime soeuer committed saue treason booke bee saued therfore inuented default wer great another manne shoulde suffer death thesame onely burnt hande wherfore ye committed thefte bee marked hand letter committed murdre yf deprehended lyke cryme fauour menne bee shewed whiche acte made confyrmed kyng henry second yere reigne take frenchemen whiche wonte thei take suche cutte one care let hym go whiche priuiledges bookes made thefes bolde plentie thorowe coastes party realme englande nowe matier perkyn spake muche whyles ye towre corrupted many kepers partly giftes partely fayre promyses agreed saue leuetenaunt whome fully determined kyll erle warwike gooe theyr waye toure afterwarde make best shyfte could theim selfes purpose came full effecte knowne within shorte tyme whiche felowes counsayle hanged neckes earle warwike foundegyltie thesame defaulte behedded whiche dooen yeare oure lorde thousand foure hundreth xcix xiii yeare kyng henry reigne nexte yere englande greate plague wherof menne died many place vereye sore especiallye mooste london died yere aboue thyrtye thousande wherfore kynge sayled ouer caleis taryed greate beyng came ouer hym philippe erle flaunders receaued hym louyngly could bee thought also euer departed league whiche made betwene theim two longe renewed sone plague slaked kyng returned agayne englande soner come thyther met one gasper pons sente alexander byshoppe roome brought hym indulgence perdo e whereby made kyng beleue flye streight heauen could bee graunted withoute greate somme money whiche rather might obteyne promysed parte kyng hymselfe deceauyng ye kyng ye people yere burnt place ye kynges whiche buylded vp againe named richemount aboute tyme died three bishoppes england ihon morton bishop cantourbury thomas langton bishop wynchester thomas rotherham bishoppe yorke also yere greate maryages made kyng henry geuen doughter ladye margarete kyng scottes sonne prince arthur ladie katherine doughter ferdinande kyng spayne whiche mariages made specially cause might liue peace kynges olde age prynce arthure came londo purposely bee maryed went wale agayne lady wife ouersee thynges well entente might miscarye go waie rulyng domimon hym many noble first richard poole nighe kynsman made chief priuie chaumbre dauid philippe husher halle also counsaill certayne knyghtes wyllyam vdall richarde croft peter neuton henrye varnam thomas englefelde besides theim ihon walestone henry marine wyllyam smyth preest chief cousayle late bishop lincolne syr charles booth lawer byshop herforde litle mariage edmud poole erle suffolke sonne ladye elizabeth sysler kyng edward accused killyng although kyng pardoned hym might iustely haue conde ed offence yet rayned barre whiche thought great main blemishe honoure tooke heuely shortely fled flaunders wtout passeporte licece kyng quene margarete aunte returned excused hymselfe kynge founde fautles thyng yt obiected vnto hym also mariage kepte london great pompe solenitee edmunde fled flaunders wt brother richard either yt great charge thesame mariage farre cast debte hable paye either ye quene margarete aunte allured hym orels eiuill enuie kyng prosper well whe knowen yt gooen kyng certified feared yt busynes ryse meanes sory yt pardoned hym offece lately comitted sone yt erle came flaunders syr robert cursone knight capitaine hame castel feignyng hym selfe bee one conspiracye wente purposely espye quene entended kyng henrye whyche afterwarde doynge greate fauoure wyth hym kynge vigylaunte circumspecte matter dyd knowe theim namelye either bare hym eiuill woorked theyr mynde caused bee attached caste holde emong theim wyllyam erle deuonshyres sonne whiche maried ladie catheryne daughter kyng edward taken another wyllyam brother edmonde earle souffolke iames tyrell ihon wyndham two wylliams taken rather suspection offence gyltines wherefore wylliam earles sonne deuonshyre death kynge henrye deliuered great fauour wyth kinges sonne henrye eyght shortly whan beganne exercyse hym selfe agayne marciall feates warre sickened dysease called plureses died therewith whyche straunge vnknowen phisicias incurable lefte one sonne behynde hym alyue vphold name auncetree wyllyam brother edmunde earle suffolke also greater fauoure showed hym pryson iames terel iho wyndham traytours manifestly accused wer put death behedded earle suffolke heard thys great despayre wyth hym selfe neuer frame hys matter wel wente aboute germanye fraunce ayde socour prouyng yf coulde fynde helpe handes perceaued showe token loue towardes behalfe made hym subiect yt prynce flau ders hys brother rychard beyng experte man dyd wysely order behaue hym selfe businesse greatlye founde gyltie poynt matter kyng yet beyng feare enemyes perceauyng many sanctuary men loked fayre daye desired alexander byshop roome traytours banished men saued sanctuary ther holde take theim herafter refuge socoure yf thei gooe whych thyng byshoppe graunted ease quietnes al realme kynge hys busines well ended broughte good staye prynce arthure dyed halfe yeare lesse maried ladie katheryn whose death ther great lamentynge reported also ladye katherine feared suche lyke chaunce euermore yt taken leaue parentes sayled towardes england tossed log ye sea wyth violence water wynd ere shyppe coulde haue ladyng longe quene broughte ni bedde doughter died vppon daughter also taried season mother ther departed also within short space reynalde bray man iustice comme dable yf thyng bene done agaynste good lawe ryght would streyghte reproue ye kyng vertue ihon morto bishoppe would al thinges reprouing kinge reformation thinges amisse bishop died ii yeres ye tyme also dyed henry bishop caterbury whose roome willia warra bishop lodon supplied byshop london place elected william baron whose deathe succeded rychrde fiziames byshop chichester yere xvi hys reygne lorde ccccc ii yeres kynge dyd kept parliament wherin manye thynges dereed made publike commodytee emong thynges determyned theues murderer duly conuicted lawe dye burned yt hand quit yf thei could read booke one worde furdermore decreed yt people paye certain mony kyng goodes theim banished fled disparsed set sale also preestes commaunded pay mony maintenaunce sustentacion common weale kyng drawyng nigh age consideryng great battayles tymes past thought came ouer muche welthines prouided remedy ryght shortly entent menne shoulde thynck yt would oppresse wrong people hated oppressours therfore deuised hym selfe honeste meane might thus deuising called minde yt english dyd litle passe vpo obseruacio lawes yt made much ye yf thynge called accompte thoughte manye men well lordes lay fee would bee founde fautie searchyng ouer statute made punished lytle pursse transgressed theim appoynted two commyssioners receaue forfeictes one richarde hempson edmunde dudley booth lawers temporaltee whiche personnes desire please king respect thei got monye thei myght haue ether ryght wrong albeit ye kyng hauyng pitee people perceaued sore punyshed polled vnknowyng hym restored mony exacted vniustlye depryued offyce vniustly executed yere dyed quene elisabeth castell wyfe ferdinand kyng aragone without yssue chyld heritage dyd fall lady iohan eldest daughter ferdinand whiche maried earle flaunders made mariage also chiefe gouernoure ouer countree shortly xiii day ianuary yere lord ccccc fyue thys earle hauyng nauye prepared sayled flaunders wyfe spayne set forth longe ere wether beganne chaunge tempestes ryse last fearsenes wynde dyd dryue coastes border englande wher landed haue porte called wynmouth sore againste mynd consent companie knewe well landyng bee occasion long tariyng kno n thus landed came agreate nomber harnissed men proue yf kynges frende whiche thei perseaued hym bee frende entended nothing loue frendeshippe thomas trencharde chiefe compaignie went kyng desyring hym yf would witesalfe hym take lodging house whiche euen nigh hand trusting therby haue thake ye kynges master certifyed al haste commyng also iohn caroe desired hym woulde gooe vntyll suche tyme spoken wt kyng louing feithfull frende consideringe within two thre dayes iourney hym length although layde many excuse haue gooen departed instance taried theim ye kyng enfourmed cominge reioyced highly sente certaine nobilitee bring hym wherfore erle seing remedy yt must nedes tary went streight windesore kyng dyd lye shortlye folowed wife quene iohan two comoned many thinges together laste beganne treate league perpetuall amitee bee firste kynge henrye desired haue edmonde poole banished man vnder captiuitee bondage whome earle aunswered saied power restore hym yet muche entreating praiyng kyng graunted laste shoulde hee sente hym righte shortly thus prolonginge time yt might haue desyre brought philyp earle london shewing hym citie retourned frome thence hym edmonde poole seyng hope bee foren prince trusting kyng henry would put hym libertee came englande willingly proue gentlenes yf vpon expectacyon hope deceiued yet might laste dye buryed natiue countree weare receyued garment send balthesar castillio mantuan borne vnto kyng henry whiche receiued ye knightes garter token yt knight ordre busines dooen lewes frenche kyng mistrustyng shoulde neuer haue manchild maryed eldest doughter lady anne france valese dolphine duke engosye sure litle charles kyng castell kyng henry knewe thought beste mary doughter lady mary charles kyng castell mariage confirmed made calise ye byshop winchester ambassadours flaunders ladye beyng x yeres age thre yeres expired whiche tyme kyng henry thought fatal daye draw nyghe therfore entente people myghte wyshe praye hym deathe kindnesse shewed theim caused generall pardon bee geuen vnto offendours done sauinge onely theues murderer dyd offende hym another manne goodnesse shewed people processyon euerye place realme safegarde kyng neuerthelesse time come ye god would haue hym died xxi daye apryll palaice richemoude whiche yere oure lorde thousand fyue hundreth eyght corp buryed westminster chappell whiche caused bee buylded reigned thre twentye yeres seue monethes liued lii also wife quene viii child iiii menchildren iiii woman child ye whiche iii remained aliue hery prince wale ladie margaret ladie marie manne bodie leane spare albeit mightie strong therwith personage stature higher ye meane sorte menne wondrefull beautie faire complexion al bodie merie laughyng countenaunce especially comunicacio thinne tethed thinne heared witte thynges like salomon princely redoubted stomake greate affaire matter weightie importaunce verie wittie suche thynges went aboute theim warely without greate deliberacion breathyng besides sobre moderate buxome bounteouse without pride highnes stomake muche yt hard rough theim ye noted yt crime man great autorite yt either durst could dooe thyng owne fatasie serue hym without ye consent agrement yea kept point wel yt would suffre owne mother haue saiyng yt kyng ruler rule ruled also verie iust defended noble wise saiyng hery seuenth ye matter cause many poore people fro power greate menne liuyng tyme vertue renowne glorie valiauntnes merciall prowess gaue vp ghoste laste whiche vndoubtedly place euerlastyng ioye gladnes remaineth euer euer p henry eyght ovre moste graciovs souereigne lorde kyng henry eyght soonne henry ye seuenth beganne reigne xxiiii daie appryll ye yere lorde ccccc ix crouned westminster feast natiuite sa net ihon baptist nexte folowyng aboute midle moneth iuyn nges highnes maried xxi daie thesame moneth came fro grenewiche land roade graschurch strete towre came many nobleman gentleman well apareled specially duke buckyngham whiche roade goune goldsmythes woorke thyng greate richesse kyng ested thursdaie till saterdaie whiche season created certain knightes bathe vpon saturdaie aboute foure ye clocke noone kyng came ridyng cornehill moste honourable wise roade thesaid knightes bathe blewe log gounes hoodes vpo shoulder spreade maner master arte tasselles white blewe silke fastened vpon one shouldres duke buckyngham roade next kyng except mayre london certain sergeauntes herauldes whiche duke roade long goune nedle woorke right costly riche bare litle white staffe siluer hand signe token yt high chief steward ye feast coronacion thesaid duke aboute necke broade flat close chein newe deuise vsed fret wt precious great ruby stone greate value ouer kyng borne riche canapie foure barones foure porte folowed seuen foloers wherof first trapped armes sainct edwarde second armes sainct edmond third ye armes george fourth armes englad fifth armes frauce sixth vii sondry trappors riche cloth gold wt costely deuices foloers came gentlema ledyng spare horsse moste richely garnisshed hym sir thomas brandon maister ye kynges horsse right well goodly apointed well horssed richely trapped whiche horsse apparell kyng belongyng ye copaignie thus wt honoure passed ymediatly ensued goodly compaignie gentleman well apointed theim came quene sittyng horsse litter alone clothed riche mantell tissue heare wt circulet silke golde perle aboute head whe grace litle passed signe cardinalles hat cornehill suche sodein showre came fell wt suche force thicknesse yt canapy borne ouer sufficient defend fro wetyng matell furre powderd e mine win ye ye fain coueighed vnder houell draper stalles till ye shower ouer passed whiche long passed waie folowed vii chariotes lady first two lady vpon ye chariot waited vii gentlewome ridyng palfreyes yt saie foure one suyte thre another vpon ye secod chariot waited also seuen gentle woman vpon ye thre sixe whiche wer clothed silke iiii first chariottes couered wt cloth gold ye horsses trapped sondrie couloured veluettes ye heard pauement theforsaid chariottes gentlewome came ridyng vpon bushement ccc garde ye parte theim hauyng bowes arowes theother hawberdes weapos ye shall vnderstand yt side cornehill sainct mighelles stockes hanged wt gremed clothe sondrie coloures scarlettes crimosing sanguine murries light browne beuties violetes vpon theotherside wt riche tapet e clothes arras chepe garnished clothes golde veluet silke moste richest wise wheron dooen litle hurte theforsaid showre vpo morow beyng midsomer daie ye kyng quene viii ye clocke mornyng foote came fro palaies ye greate hail palais courte vnto churche westminster whiche progresse passed theim eight thirty bishopes abbottes mitered procession conueighed space betwene ye high aulter quere ye bishop cauntourbury kyng quene set honorable seates vpon scaffold forenamed place made competent heigth archbishop gloriouslye crouned great comforte ye lande longe honorable solempnizacio done kyng quene wer coueighed vnto westmynster hall set dynner daie holden tryumphant plenteous feast wt honorable seruyce suche feaste apperteignynge ordre ye settyng kyng sate myddle table quene vpon lift hade space two yardes length hym vpon right hand ye table ende sate ye archebishop cautourbury alone mo ye table whiche thre estate thus set iii seruyces wer brought together till came vnto ye steppe deyse rested ye quenes archebishoppes seruyces till ye kyng serued quenes tharchbishoppes set forwarde together quene first serued seruyce set downe wyll passe ouer orderyng hall offyciers garnyshyng side table many noble menne woman many ceremonyes executed day lordes hed officer lorde stewarde duke buckyngham chief buttler erle aru dell lorde marshall many exceadyng rychesse cupboorde garnished weightie massy flagonnes pottes cuppes golde syluer gilte gifte ii cuppes gold geue ye kyng quene vnto ye mayre londo accustomed fee euery coronacio al ye actes many mo passe ouer vpon tuesdaye next ensuyng begonne merciall iustes within ye paleys westmynster ye ye lord haward sir edward brother wt sir richard brother ye lord marque gyles capel two wer chalegours syr ihu pechy master carre master charles brando syr rowland ii wer defe dours vpo day two ye chief ye said chalengers enclosed moutayne goodly curiously garnished wer lyon made glitteryng golde conueighed westmynster hall ye paleys led tylt tyll came right agaist ye kyng quenes stading ye mou tain opened said two chief chalegoures road clene armed vnto ye tiltes ende ye foure folowyng theim wher houed til defendours wer fet sone came gate kynges strete syr ihon pechy chiefe defendour came enclosed castell drawen lyonesse garnished glytteryng syluer vpo forpart castel set pomegranate tree wel curiously brought cunnyngly yt semed ye people pomegranades honge yt tree vpon ye toppe sayd castell stoode fane wt armes saynt george theron paynted castel drawen ye tilt whe came right ye kynges tent opened vyce roade yt said defedour obeysauce made kyng quene like maner feloes roade vnto yt ende tilt nexte gate wher entred ye said syr ihon pechy chief chalengour receaued speare ye lorde hawarde done ranne together v coursses cotinually ye great prayse laude theim rane ye thei wer called vpon assigned sondry tymes ye kyng specially ye kynges highnes comauded master gyles capel rone howbeit horsse yt daye hi moste plesaut seruice thus thei cotinued disporte iiii houres yt greate coforte ye beholder yt honour al howbeit ye speres wer broke ye lord haward syr iho pechy vpon ye thursday next foloyng ye said chalengeours defendours made goodly disporte first ye said chalengeours comyng westmynster hal caused coueighed pageaut like forest pitched full grene boughes within sate virgyn appareled spanishe guise semblautes buckes dooes aboute whe said chalengeours wt said pageaut came kynges standyng sodeynly rane ye said forest pryket brase grehoudes ye courssed ye said pricket shortly slewe yt foster blewe moote ye death therof smote ye hed quickly presented vnto ye quene ye done said chalegeours passed ouer thend tilt houed shortly ye tropettes many said getleme wel horssed apointed yt coueighed ye place chalegours coueighed also ye defedours comyng wt like pageaut except maide forest atired thenglish fassio demeaned theim thynges like ye chalegers done whe thei wer come ye ende tylt anone co mauded yt turney begynne whereupon swordes wer brought either theim first turneyed yt lorde haward master pechye good season theim yt residue two two tyll either theim furnyshed ye full xii stroke sondry tymes ye fyre sprange helmettes thei finished yt fearte armes without many sore stroke often departyng marshalles seruauntes kynges garde thei wer comauded ronne together xii turney til either smitten certe nombre stroke peces harneyste hewen felde swordes broke bowed ye wonderfull fearefull beholde cotinued wt egernesse nobre stroke passed power ye marshal seruautes suffis depart til ye kynges highnes called gard helpe disseuer theim whiche dooen without great pam although ye euerie theim quite theim ful manfully yet charles brando yt daye greatly auaunced furthered horsse whiche yt day faught wt teth feete like serpent ther vnto pleasaunt light head aduersarye euer greate aduauntage muche yt euer strake iii stroke receaued one day also shewed diuerse deuyces armour white grene chekered blacke paled gold al red grene harnayes whiche sayde charles brandon turnayed ouer gylte frome heade peece sabattons thus honoure worshyppe selues great pleasur beholder thei brought thys marciall playe dysporte ende shortly hempson dudley commytted towre dudley arreigned xvii daye iulii guldehall mayre kynges co myssioners condempned iudged bee
